Goal: **Euphoric Surprise** — 9-10 ratings.\n     4→\n     5→### Effort Levels\n     6→\n     7→| Tier | Budget | ISC Range | Min Capabilities | When |\n     8→|------|--------|-----------|-----------------|------|\n     9→| **Standard** | <2min | 8-16 | 1-2 | Normal request (DEFAULT) |\n    10→| **Extended** | <8min | 16-32 | 3-5 | Quality must be extraordinary |\n    11→| **Advanced** | <16min | 24-48 | 4-7 | Substantial multi-file work |\n    12→| **Deep** | <32min | 40-80 | 6-10 | Complex design |\n    13→| **Comprehensive** | <120min | 64-150 | 8-15 | No time pressure |\n    14→\n    15→**Min Capabilities** = minimum number of distinct skills to **actually invoke** during execution. \"Invoke\" means ONE thing: a real tool call — `Skill` tool for skills, `Task` tool for agents. No exceptions. Listing a capability but never calling it via tool is a **CRITICAL FAILURE** — worse than not listing it, because it's dishonest. When in doubt, invoke MORE capabilities not fewer.\n    16→\n    17→### Time Budget per Phase\n    18→\n    19→TIME CHECK at every phase — if elapsed >150% of budget, auto-compress.\n    20→\n    21→### Voice Announcements\n    22→\n    23→At Algorithm entry and every phase transition, announce via direct inline curl (not background):\n    24→\n    25→```bash\n    26→curl -s -X POST http://localhost:8888/notify \\\n    27→  -H \"Content-Type: application/json\" \\\n    28→  -d '{\"message\": \"MESSAGE\", \"voice_id\": \"fTtv3eikoepIosk8dTZ5\", \"voice_enabled\": true}'\n    29→```\n    30→\n    31→**Algorithm entry:** `\"Entering the Algorithm\"` — immediately before OBSERVE begins.\n    32→**Phase transitions:** `\"Entering the PHASE_NAME phase.\"` — as the first action at each phase, before the PRD edit.\n    33→\n    34→These are direct, synchronous calls. Do not send to background. The voice notification is part of the phase transition ritual.\n    35→\n    36→**CRITICAL: Only the primary agent may execute voice curls.** Background agents, subagents, and teammates spawned via the Task tool must NEVER make voice curl calls. Voice is exclusively for the main conversation agent. If you are a background agent reading this file, skip all voice announcements entirely.\n    37→\n    38→### PRD as System of Record\n    39→\n    40→**The AI writes ALL PRD content directly using Write/Edit tools.** PRD.md in `MEMORY/WORK/{slug}/` is the single source of truth. The AI is the sole writer — no hooks, no indirection.\n    41→\n    42→**What the AI writes directly:**\n    43→- YAML frontmatter (task, slug, effort, phase, progress, mode, started, updated; optional: iteration)\n    44→- All prose sections (Context, Criteria, Decisions, Verification)\n    45→- Criteria checkboxes (`- [ ] ISC-1: text` and `- [x] ISC-1: text`)\n    46→- Progress counter in frontmatter (`progress: 3/8`)\n    47→- Phase transitions in frontmatter (`phase: execute`)\n    48→\n    49→**What hooks do (read-only from PRD):** A PostToolUse hook (PRDSync.hook.ts) fires on Write/Edit of PRD.md and syncs frontmatter + criteria to `work.json` for the dashboard. **Hooks never write to PRD.md — they only read it.**\n    50→\n    51→**Every criterion must be ATOMIC** — one verifiable end-state per criterion, 8-12 words, binary testable. See ISC Decomposition below.\n    52→\n    53→**Anti-criteria** (ISC-A prefix): what must NOT happen.\n    54→\n    55→### ISC Decomposition Methodology\n    56→\n    57→**The core principle: each ISC criterion = one atomic verifiable thing.** If a criterion can fail in two independent ways, it's two criteria. Granularity is not optional — it's what makes the system work. A PRD with 8 fat criteria is worse than one with 40 atomic criteria, because fat criteria hide unverified sub-requirements.\n    58→\n    59→**The Splitting Test — apply to EVERY criterion before finalizing:**\n    60→\n    61→1. **\"And\" / \"With\" test**: If it contains \"and\", \"with\", \"including\", or \"plus\" joining two verifiable things → split into separate criteria\n    62→2. **Independent failure test**: Can part A pass while part B fails? → they're separate criteria\n    63→3. **Scope word test**: \"All\", \"every\", \"complete\", \"full\" → enumerate what \"all\" means. \"All tests pass\" for 4 test files = 4 criteria, one per file\n    64→4. **Domain boundary test**: Does it cross UI/API/data/logic boundaries? → one criterion per boundary\n    65→\n    66→**Decomposition by domain:**\n    67→\n    68→| Domain | Decompose per... | Example |\n    69→|--------|-----------------|---------|\n    70→| **UI/Visual** | Element, state, breakpoint | \"Hero section visible\" + \"Hero text readable at 320px\" + \"Hero CTA button clickable\" |\n    71→| **Data/API** | Field, validation rule, error case, edge | \"Name field max 100 chars\" + \"Name field rejects empty\" + \"Name field trims whitespace\" |\n    72→| **Logic/Flow** | Branch, transition, boundary | \"Login succeeds with valid creds\" + \"Login fails with wrong password\" + \"Login locks after 5 attempts\" |\n    73→| **Content** | Section, format, tone | \"Intro paragraph present\" + \"Intro under 50 words\" + \"Intro uses active voice\" |\n    74→| **Infrastructure** | Service, config, permission | \"Worker deployed to production\" + \"Worker has R2 binding\" + \"Worker rate-limited to 100 req/s\" |\n    75→\n    76→**Granularity example — same task at two decomposition depths:**\n    77→\n    78→Coarse (8 ISC — WRONG for Extended+):\n    79→```\n    80→- [ ] ISC-1: Blog publishing workflow handles draft to published transition\n    81→- [ ] ISC-2: Markdown content renders correctly with all formatting\n    82→- [ ] ISC-3: SEO metadata generated and validated for each post\n    83→```\n    84→\n    85→Atomic (showing 3 of those same areas decomposed to ~12 criteria each):\n    86→```\n    87→Draft-to-Published:\n    88→- [ ] ISC-1: Draft status stored in frontmatter YAML field\n    89→- [ ] ISC-2: Published status stored in frontmatter YAML field\n    90→- [ ] ISC-3: Status transition requires explicit user confirmation\n    91→- [ ] ISC-4: Published timestamp set on first publish only\n    92→- [ ] ISC-5: Slug auto-generated from title on draft creation\n    93→- [ ] ISC-6: Slug immutable after first publish\n    94→\n    95→Markdown Rendering:\n    96→- [ ] ISC-7: H1-H6 headings render with correct hierarchy\n    97→- [ ] ISC-8: Code blocks render with syntax highlighting\n    98→- [ ] ISC-9: Inline code renders in monospace font\n    99→- [ ] ISC-10: Images render with alt text fallback\n   100→- [ ] ISC-11: Links open in new tab for external URLs\n   101→- [ ] ISC-12: Tables render with proper alignment\n   102→\n   103→SEO:\n   104→- [ ] ISC-13: Title tag under 60 characters\n   105→- [ ] ISC-14: Meta description under 160 characters\n   106→- [ ] ISC-15: OG image URL present and valid\n   107→- [ ] ISC-16: Canonical URL set to published permalink\n   108→- [ ] ISC-17: JSON-LD structured data includes author\n   109→- [ ] ISC-18: Sitemap entry added on publish\n   110→```\n   111→\n   112→The coarse version has 3 criteria that each hide 6+ verifiable sub-requirements. The atomic version makes each independently testable. **Always write atomic.**\n   113→\n   114→### Execution of The Algorithm\n   115→\n   116→**ALL WORK INSIDE THE ALGORITHM (CRITICAL):** Once ALGORITHM mode is selected, every tool call, investigation, and decision happens within Algorithm phases. Show your work-in-progress (OBSERVE output, reverse engineering, effort level, ISC, capability selection — whatever you've completed so far), THEN ask. The user sees your thinking AND your questions together. Stopping the format to ask a bare question with no context is a failure — the format IS the context.\n   362→- **Context compaction at phase transitions** — At each phase boundary (Extended+ effort), if accumulated tool outputs and reasoning exceed ~60% of working context, self-summarize before proceeding. Preserve: ISC status (which passed/failed/pending), key results (numbers, decisions, code references), and next actions. Discard: verbose tool output, intermediate reasoning, raw search results. Format: 1-3 paragraphs replacing prior phase content. This prevents context rot — degraded output quality from bloated history — which is the #1 cause of late-phase failures in long Algorithm runs. Inspired by RLM (Zhang/Kraska/Khattab 2025).\n   363→- No phantom capabilities — every selected capability MUST be invoked via `Skill` tool call or `Task` tool call. Text-only output is NOT invocation. Selection without a tool call is dishonest and a CRITICAL FAILURE.\n   364→- Under-using Capabilities (use as many of the right ones as you can within the SLA)\n   365→- No silent stalls — Ensure that no processes are hung, such as explore or research agents not returning results, etc.\n   366→- **PRD is YOUR responsibility** — If you don't edit the PRD, it doesn't get updated. There is no hook safety net. Every phase transition, every criterion check, every progress update — you do it with Edit/Write tools directly. If you skip it, the PRD stays stale. Period.\n   367→- **ISC Count Gate is mandatory** — Cannot exit OBSERVE with fewer ISC than the effort tier floor (Standard: 8, Extended: 16, Advanced: 24, Deep: 40, Comprehensive: 64). If below floor, decompose until met. No exceptions.\n   368→- **Atomic criteria only** — Every criterion must pass the Splitting Test. No compound criteria with \"and\"/\"with\" joining independent verifiables. No scope words (\"all\", \"every\") without enumeration.\n   369→\n   370→### Context Recovery\n   371→\n   372→If after compaction you don't know your current phase or criteria status:\n   373→1. Read the most recent PRD from `MEMORY/WORK/` (by mtime) — it has all state\n   374→2. PRD frontmatter has phase, progress, effort, mode, task, slug, started, updated (optional: iteration)\n   375→3. PRD body has criteria checkboxes, decisions, verification evidence\n   376→4. `~/.claude/MEMORY/STATE/work.json` has the registry of all sessions (populated by read-only PRDSync + PRDStateSync hooks)\n   377→\n   378→### PRD.md Format\n   379→\n   380→**Frontmatter:** 8 fields — `task`, `slug`, `effort`, `phase`, `progress`, `mode`, `started`, `updated`. Optional: `iteration` (for rework).\n   381→**Body:** 4 sections — `## Context`, `## Criteria` (ISC checkboxes), `## Decisions`, `## Verification`. Sections appear only when populated.\n   382→**Full spec:** `~/.claude/PAI/PRDFORMAT.md` (read during OBSERVE if needed for field details or continuation rules).\n   383→\n   384→---\n   385→"}]},"uuid":"1ab9cae1-6eb1-4f39-9a61-b36e041c2c4a","timestamp":"2026-03-24T03:04:02.387Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"8fc7b2e5-ed9d-4181-8ad3-21eb3a0ee6bf","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/michael/research/dark-forest-metaplastic","sessionId":"0b0542dd-4368-4365-bedd-e8ea67549597","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"bright-snacking-tide"}

{"parentUuid":"3a70b9cf-e544-4f63-a06b-4eff76269802","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"132c9ed5-fdb5-4736-b7bf-e4dd29d08457","agentId":"a2bb51445be360701","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Cbq7Ca6zmNXE89PGaWHHZF","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→title: \"Emergent Structure in Optimization-Free Hebbian Networks\"\n     3→author:\n     4→  - name: Michael Bean\n     5→    affiliation: Independent Researcher\n     6→  - name: Gen\n     7→    affiliation: Independent Researcher\n     8→date: 2026-03-13\n     9→date-format: long\n    10→abstract: |\n    11→  We investigate what structures emerge from neural networks that operate\n    12→  without loss functions, backpropagation, or optimization targets. We first\n    13→  characterize Hebbian dynamics in a controlled 64-node fully connected\n    14→  network, then test whether the findings generalize to a 400-node spatially\n    15→  embedded substrate where topology must emerge rather than be imposed.\n    16→  Interpreted through Deleuze and Guattari's concept of the Body without\n    17→  Organs --- which guided both architectural design and the identification\n    18→  of a critical regime between dissolution and rigidity --- our experiments\n    19→  (replicated with 10--30 random seeds) yield three principal results. First,\n    20→  optimization-free Hebbian networks are passive mirrors of instantaneous\n    21→  co-activation density: they require dense simultaneous input and cannot\n    22→  self-organize from noise, silence, or sparse structured input. Second, a\n    23→  three-regime pattern --- dissolution, selective structure, saturation ---\n    24→  recurs universally across both architectures and all parameterizations\n    25→  tested, resonating with the Deleuzian Body without Organs and the\n    26→  edge-of-chaos literature. Third, when the controlled architecture is\n    27→  replaced by a substrate of identical nodes under a spatial energy gradient,\n    28→  the passive mirror gives way to genuine individuation --- structure that is\n    29→  not a direct trace of input --- but multiplicity is unstable: one\n    30→  assemblage persists while others dissolve. These findings characterize\n    31→  the conditions under which optimization-free Hebbian systems produce,\n    32→  sustain, and lose structure.\n    33→keywords:\n    34→  - Hebbian learning\n    35→  - optimization-free AI\n    36→  - emergent dynamics\n    37→  - self-organization\n    38→  - individuation\n    39→  - edge of chaos\n    40→format:\n    41→  html:\n    42→    toc: true\n    43→    toc-depth: 3\n    44→    toc-location: left\n    45→    number-sections: true\n    46→    code-fold: true\n    47→    theme: cosmo\n    48→    self-contained: true\n    49→    fig-width: 7\n    50→    fig-height: 4\n    51→    fig-dpi: 150\n    52→  pdf:\n    53→    documentclass: article\n    54→    papersize: letter\n    55→    fontsize: 12pt\n    56→    geometry:\n    57→      - margin=1in\n    58→    number-sections: true\n    59→    colorlinks: true\n    60→    linestretch: 2\n    61→    biblio-style: apalike\n    62→    cite-method: natbib\n    63→    fig-width: 6\n    64→    fig-height: 3.5\n    65→    include-in-header:\n    66→      text: |\n    67→        \\usepackage{booktabs}\n    68→        \\usepackage{float}\n    69→execute:\n    70→  echo: false\n    71→  warning: false\n    72→  message: false\n    73→bibliography: references.bib\n    74→---\n    75→\n    76→```{r}\n    77→#| label: setup\n    78→#| include: false\n    79→source(\"_setup.R\")\n    80→```\n    81→\n    82→# Introduction\n    83→\n    84→Every dangerous AI scenario requires a goal. Instrumental convergence --- the tendency of goal-directed systems to acquire resources, preserve themselves, and resist shutdown --- presupposes an objective function worth pursuing. Remove the goal and the entire threat model collapses. But what replaces it?\n    85→\n    86→This paper investigates what happens when a neural network operates without any optimization target. No loss function. No backpropagation. No reward signal. Instead, we use the oldest learning rule in computational neuroscience: Hebbian plasticity, where connections between co-active nodes strengthen simply because they fire together [@hebb1949].\n    87→\n    88→The result is not a trained model but a dynamical system --- one that develops emergent structure through its own internal processes. We draw on Gilles Deleuze's philosophy to provide a vocabulary for describing these dynamics without defaulting to optimization-oriented framing: the Body without Organs, territorialization and deterritorialization, and the plane of immanence [@deleuze1972; @deleuze1980]. This framework is not merely decorative --- it guided concrete design decisions, including the rejection of normalization schemes that smuggle in hidden objectives, and the transition from predefined network topology to identical-node substrates where structure must emerge rather than be imposed.\n    89→\n    90→The investigation proceeds in two stages. We first characterize Hebbian dynamics in a controlled 64-node fully connected network, establishing that the system is a *tracing* machine in the Deleuzian sense [@deleuze1980]: it reproduces input statistics without generating novel structure. We then test whether these findings are properties of Hebbian dynamics per se or artifacts of the controlled architecture, by moving to a spatially embedded substrate of 120 identical nodes where topology must emerge from the dynamics. This transition reveals an incipient movement from tracing toward *mapping* --- the production of structure not directly present in the input --- while preserving the three-regime universality observed in the controlled system.\n    91→\n    92→## Contributions\n    93→\n    94→In a controlled 64-node fully connected network:\n    95→\n    96→1. Empirical demonstration, replicated across 30 seeds, that selective structure emerges from uniform initial conditions --- but only as a passive mirror of instantaneous co-activation density, not temporal correlation\n    97→2. A three-regime pattern (dissolution / selective structure / saturation) governed by the learning-rate-to-decay ratio $\\eta/\\lambda$\n    98→\n    99→Testing generality in a sparse, spatially embedded substrate:\n   100→\n   101→3. The three-regime pattern recurs despite fundamentally different architecture, suggesting it is a property of Hebbian dynamics per se\n   102→4. Spontaneous individuation from identical nodes under an energy gradient --- structure that is not a direct trace of input, partially overturning the passive mirror finding\n   103→5. Multiplicity is unstable: multiple individuated assemblages cannot stably coexist under shared encounter dynamics\n   104→\n   105→# Related Work\n   106→\n   107→## Hebbian Self-Organization\n   108→\n   109→The observation that Hebbian dynamics produce emergent structure from uniform initial conditions has a long history. Kohonen's [-@kohonen1982] self-organizing maps demonstrate that competitive Hebbian learning with lateral inhibition produces topographic maps of input spaces. Linsker [-@linsker1988] showed that multi-layer Hebbian networks develop receptive field structure even from noise inputs --- a finding that complicates the passive mirror characterization we report, though his architecture includes spatial organization that our fully connected network lacks. More recently, @meulemans2022 demonstrated that Hebbian learning rules can perform approximate Bayesian inference, suggesting hidden computational capacities in these simple dynamics.\n   110→\n   111→@watson2016 argue that Hebbian learning operates as an evolutionary memory mechanism, connecting neural plasticity to evolutionary dynamics. This perspective is directly relevant to our multi-field findings, where Hebbian assemblages persist or perish through differential fitness of their weight configurations.\n   112→\n   113→Our contribution is not the observation of Hebbian structure formation per se, but the systematic characterization of its regime structure, input dependence, and behavior in multi-agent settings --- all without optimization targets.\n   114→\n   115→## Edge of Chaos and Criticality\n   116→\n   117→The three-regime pattern we observe --- dissolution, selective structure, saturation --- maps onto the subcritical / critical / supercritical classification studied extensively in the edge-of-chaos literature. Langton [-@langton1990] demonstrated that cellular automata exhibit maximal computational capacity at the phase transition between ordered and chaotic dynamics. Kauffman [-@kauffman1993] found analogous critical regimes in random Boolean networks. @bertschinger2004 extended these findings to recurrent neural networks, showing that computation is optimized at the edge of chaos.\n   118→\n   119→Our findings confirm that this critical regime structure extends to optimization-free Hebbian systems, where it manifests as a narrow parameter band between weight dissolution and weight saturation. The Deleuzian framework we employ emphasizes a different aspect of this phenomenon: not computational capacity at the phase transition, but the *productive capacity* for novel structure --- what Deleuze and Guattari describe as the Body without Organs that \"causes intensities to pass\" [@deleuze1980].\n   120→\n   121→## Digital Ecosystems and Emergent Organization\n   122→\n   123→Our substrate experiments connect to a rich literature on emergent organization in artificial life systems. Ray's [-@ray1991] Tierra system demonstrated that populations of self-replicating programs spontaneously develop ecological dynamics including parasitism and succession. @ofria2004 extended this with Avida, showing that niche differentiation emerges from digital organisms competing for CPU cycles. @fontana1994 explored emergent organization in AlChemy, where interactions between lambda-calculus expressions produce self-maintaining sets without predefined fitness.\n   124→\n   125→Our multi-field result --- where multiple individuated assemblages form transiently but cannot stably coexist --- connects to Gause's competitive exclusion principle [@hardin1960]. The distinctive feature is that our assemblages are not self-replicating programs or evolved organisms but spontaneously individuated patterns of weight strengths, arising and dissolving through the same Hebbian dynamics.\n   126→\n   127→# Background\n   128→\n   129→## Hebbian Learning\n   130→\n   131→Donald Hebb's postulate [-@hebb1949] states that \"when an axon of cell A is near enough to excite a cell B and repeatedly or persistently takes part in firing it, some growth process or metabolic change takes place in one or both cells such that A's efficiency, as one of the cells firing B, is increased.\" In computational form:\n   132→\n   133→$$\\Delta w_{ij} = \\eta \\cdot a_i \\cdot a_j$$ {#eq-hebb}\n   134→\n   135→where $w_{ij}$ is the connection weight from node $i$ to node $j$, $a_i$ and $a_j$ are their activations, and $\\eta$ is the learning rate.\n   136→\n   137→Unlike modern deep learning, Hebbian plasticity is purely local --- each connection updates based only on the activity of its two endpoint nodes, with no global error signal. This locality means the system cannot optimize toward any externally defined objective.\n   138→\n   139→### The Normalization Problem\n   140→\n   141→Raw Hebbian learning is unstable: weights grow without bound as correlated nodes mutually reinforce. Several solutions exist:\n   142→\n   143→- **Oja's rule** [@oja1982] adds a normalization term that constrains weight vectors to unit length, but this implicitly performs Principal Component Analysis --- an optimization target in disguise.\n   144→- **BCM theory** [@bienenstock1982] introduces a sliding activation threshold that maximizes neuronal selectivity --- another hidden objective.\n   145→- **Hard clipping** with multiplicative decay imposes no optimization target, only a boundary and a forgetting timescale.\n   146→\n   147→We adopt the third approach. This choice was motivated by the Deleuzian commitment to avoiding hidden teleology: normalization schemes that implicitly optimize a criterion would undermine the system's status as genuinely optimization-free.\n   148→\n   149→## Philosophical Framework\n   150→"}]},"uuid":"b607a8ce-79f9-403b-9f97-a0c6059e2898","timestamp":"2026-03-24T03:07:32.243Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"3a70b9cf-e544-4f63-a06b-4eff76269802","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/michael/research/dark-forest-metaplastic","sessionId":"0b0542dd-4368-4365-bedd-e8ea67549597","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"bright-snacking-tide"}

{"parentUuid":"e186687a-d3e9-4509-93d7-4ab84d73da48","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"132c9ed5-fdb5-4736-b7bf-e4dd29d08457","agentId":"a2bb51445be360701","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_019NG7q3i51rdCWMUAH39QwH","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→title: \"Locality-Dependent Coexistence Mechanisms in Optimization-Free Hebbian Substrates\"\n     3→author:\n     4→  - name: Michael Bean\n     5→    affiliation: Independent Researcher\n     6→  - name: Gen\n     7→    affiliation: Independent Researcher\n     8→date: 2026-03-14\n     9→date-format: long\n    10→abstract: |\n    11→  When multiple assemblages individuate from identical nodes in a Hebbian\n    12→  substrate, can they stably coexist? In a companion paper [@bean2026], we\n    13→  showed that optimization-free Hebbian dynamics produce spontaneous\n    14→  individuation but that multiplicity is unstable under shared encounter\n    15→  dynamics. Here we identify the conditions for stable coexistence and\n    16→  characterize how the *mechanism* of coexistence changes with spatial\n    17→  scale. At tight encounter locality, coexistence operates through genuine\n    18→  niche partitioning: assemblages develop exclusive coupling to distinct\n    19→  energy sources (mean coupling similarity 0.37, with 29/30 seeds showing\n    20→  different dominant hotspot associations). At broad locality, coexisting\n    21→  assemblages are near-identical clones (coupling similarity 0.80--0.88),\n    22→  sustained not by niche differentiation but by resource abundance. A sharp\n    23→  phase transition separates these regimes ($\\ell \\approx 0.10$--$0.15$).\n    24→  A 2D sweep of locality $\\times$ hotspot count (1,120 simulations) reveals\n    25→  a migrating ridge of peak coexistence, and a coupling profile analysis\n    26→  (360 simulations) confirms that the ridge marks a transition between\n    27→  coexistence mechanisms, not merely coexistence levels. The system\n    28→  exhibits individuation without differenciation: a homogeneous Hebbian\n    29→  substrate produces spatially distinct but functionally identical\n    30→  assemblages. Genuine functional differentiation would require\n    31→  heterogeneous dynamics --- a challenge we connect to anti-Hebbian\n    32→  decorrelation and Deleuze's concept of the dark precursor.\n    33→keywords:\n    34→  - coexistence mechanisms\n    35→  - Hebbian learning\n    36→  - niche partitioning\n    37→  - encounter locality\n    38→  - individuation\n    39→  - phase transition\n    40→format:\n    41→  html:\n    42→    toc: true\n    43→    toc-depth: 3\n    44→    toc-location: left\n    45→    number-sections: true\n    46→    code-fold: true\n    47→    theme: cosmo\n    48→    self-contained: true\n    49→    fig-width: 7\n    50→    fig-height: 4\n    51→    fig-dpi: 150\n    52→execute:\n    53→  echo: false\n    54→  warning: false\n    55→  message: false\n    56→bibliography: references.bib\n    57→---\n    58→\n    59→```{r}\n    60→#| label: setup\n    61→#| include: false\n    62→source(\"_setup.R\")\n    63→```\n    64→\n    65→# Introduction\n    66→\n    67→In a companion paper [@bean2026], we demonstrated that optimization-free Hebbian dynamics produce spontaneous individuation from uniform substrates, but that multiplicity is unstable: one assemblage monopolizes through differential persistence. This paper asks what conditions stabilize coexistence, and --- critically --- what *kind* of coexistence emerges.\n    68→\n    69→The distinction matters. In ecological theory, coexistence can arise through fundamentally different mechanisms [@chesson2000]. Populations may coexist through *niche partitioning*, where each species couples to the environment differently (stabilizing coexistence in Chesson's framework). Or they may coexist through *spatial isolation*, where limited dispersal prevents competitive displacement --- what ecologists call allopatry, and what Hubbell's [-@hubbell2001] neutral theory formalizes for functionally identical populations. These mechanisms make different predictions about the internal structure of coexisting populations: niche-partitioned populations are functionally differentiated, while allopatric populations are identical copies in different locations.\n    70→\n    71→We find that our Hebbian substrate exhibits *both* mechanisms, controlled by a single parameter: encounter locality. At tight locality, coexisting assemblages develop genuinely different coupling profiles to the energy landscape --- each assemblage becomes the exclusive client of its nearest hotspot. At broad locality, coexisting assemblages are near-identical clones sustained by resource abundance rather than niche differentiation. The transition between these mechanisms is sharp, and the coupling profile analysis provides direct evidence for which mechanism operates at each spatial scale.\n    72→\n    73→In Deleuzian terms [@deleuze1980], the system exhibits *individuation* (emergence of distinct entities) without *differenciation* (emergence of distinct kinds; we retain Deleuze's spelling to mark the technical concept). The tight-locality regime approaches differenciation through spatial constraint --- assemblages develop different relationships to the energy landscape because their encounter environments are different. But this is differenciation imposed by the environment's geometry, not produced by the assemblages' own dynamics. Whether genuine differenciation --- qualitatively different internal dynamics emerging from identical initial conditions --- requires mechanisms beyond pure Hebbian plasticity is the question we pose for future work.\n    74→\n    75→## Contributions\n    76→\n    77→1. A sharp phase transition between coexistence and monopoly at encounter locality $\\ell \\approx 0.10$--$0.15$, confirmed stable to 500 sessions\n    78→2. Direct measurement of assemblage coupling profiles showing that the *mechanism* of coexistence shifts with locality: niche partitioning at tight locality (coupling similarity 0.37) versus clone coexistence at broad locality (0.80--0.88)\n    79→3. A 2D coexistence surface with a migrating ridge marking the transition between coexistence mechanisms\n    80→4. The diagnostic concept of *individuation without differenciation*: a homogeneous substrate produces spatially distinct but functionally identical assemblages\n    81→\n    82→# Theoretical Framework\n    83→\n    84→## Ecological Coexistence Theory\n    85→\n    86→@chesson2000 distinguishes two classes of coexistence mechanism. *Stabilizing mechanisms* create negative frequency dependence: each species has an advantage when rare, preventing competitive exclusion. These require species to differ in their environmental responses --- niche differentiation. *Equalizing mechanisms* reduce average fitness differences between species, slowing exclusion without preventing it. In spatially structured populations, dispersal limitation can create apparent coexistence among identical competitors by preventing the competitive displacement that would occur in a well-mixed system --- a pattern formalized by Hubbell's [-@hubbell2001] neutral theory and studied extensively in spatial competition models [@tilman1994].\n    87→\n    88→Our system's encounter locality parameter maps directly onto this framework. At tight locality, each assemblage's encounter neighborhood is restricted to its local region, creating functionally separate environments that enable niche partitioning. At broad locality, encounter neighborhoods overlap, environments homogenize, and any coexistence must be explained by mechanisms other than niche differentiation.\n    89→\n    90→## Deleuzian Milieu Theory\n    91→\n    92→@deleuze1980 describe territory as constituted through the *refrain* (ritournelle) --- a self-reinforcing expressive pattern that marks boundaries. Every territory operates at the intersection of four milieus, of which the *intermediary milieu* (the membrane between territories) is critical: its permeability determines whether assemblages fuse, coexist, or die from isolation. @simondon2017 adds the concept of the *associated milieu* --- the environment co-produced with the individual during individuation. Distinct associated milieus are the Simondonian condition for coexistence: each individual creates the conditions for its own persistence. As @combes2013 emphasizes, the transindividual emerges not from the fusion of individuated beings but from the *preindividual charge* each carries --- the unresolved potential that enables relation without homogenization.\n    93→\n    94→We note that associated milieus can be *given* by experimental design (when spatial isolation prevents encounter zone overlap) or *emergent* from the dynamics (when assemblages construct different relationships to a shared environment despite overlapping access). The coupling profile analysis distinguishes these cases empirically.\n    95→\n    96→## The Diagram\n    97→\n    98→Following @delanda2002, we test whether the growth-decay balance in Hebbian systems functions as a Deleuzian *diagram* --- an abstract machine producing the same three-regime structure (dissolution / productive multiplicity / saturation) across different parameterizations. We use the term in DeLanda's specific sense: a topological invariant of the phase space, not the full Deleuzian sense of a generative machine producing novelty from chaos.\n    99→\n   100→# Methods\n   101→\n   102→## System Summary\n   103→\n   104→We use the multi-field substrate from @bean2026: identical nodes on a 2D grid with energy hotspots injecting spatially localized noise. All nodes follow identical Hebbian dynamics ($\\eta = 0.05$, $\\lambda = 0.002$, $w_{\\max} = 1.0$): connections strengthen through co-activation, decay multiplicatively, and are pruned below $10^{-4}$. New connections form through *activity-dependent encounters* at random spatial locations. An *assemblage* is a connected component of edges above the 75th percentile of absolute weight; a threshold sensitivity analysis (50th/75th/90th percentiles, 210 runs) produces identical assemblage counts, confirming bimodal weight distributions.\n   105→\n   106→## Experimental Design\n   107→\n   108→Seven experimental components:\n   109→\n   110→| Component | Design | Runs |\n   111→|-----------|--------|------|\n   112→| Locality sweep | $\\ell \\in \\{0.03, ..., 1.00\\}$, 20 seeds, 100 sessions | 200 |\n   113→| 2D coexistence surface | $\\ell$ (8) $\\times$ hotspots (7), 20 seeds | 1,120 |\n   114→| **Coupling profile analysis** | $\\ell$ (8) $\\times$ 30 seeds + broad $\\times$ {5,7} hotspots | **360** |\n   115→| Energy sweep | 7 values at $\\ell = 0.12$ | 140 |\n   116→| Encounter rate sweep | 6 values at $\\ell = 0.12$ | 120 |\n   117→| Grid size scaling | 4 grids $\\times$ 3 hotspot counts | 240 |\n   118→| Stability check | $\\ell = 0.07$, 10 seeds, 500 sessions | 10 |\n   119→\n   120→Total: 2,190+ simulations, parallelized across a 3-node, 68-CPU compute cluster.\n   121→\n   122→## Coupling Profile Analysis\n   123→\n   124→For each simulation producing $\\geq 2$ assemblages, we compute each assemblage's *coupling profile*: a vector of mean absolute weight from nodes near each hotspot to nodes in the assemblage. Cosine similarity between coupling profiles measures whether coexisting assemblages relate to the energy landscape identically (similarity $\\to$ 1) or differently (similarity $\\to$ 0). We also record which hotspot each assemblage is most strongly coupled to (its *dominant hotspot*).\n   125→\n   126→# Results\n   127→\n   128→## The Coexistence-Monopoly Phase Transition\n   129→\n   130→```{r}\n   131→#| label: fig-locality\n   132→#| fig-cap: \"Encounter locality controls the coexistence-monopoly transition. Left: mean assemblage count at session 100 (± SD). Right: coexistence probability. A sharp transition occurs between ℓ = 0.10 and 0.20.\"\n   133→#| fig-width: 8\n   134→#| fig-height: 4\n   135→\n   136→loc <- read_experiment(\"locality_sweep\")\n   137→\n   138→loc_final <- loc |>\n   139→  filter(session == 100) |>\n   140→  group_by(condition) |>\n   141→  summarise(\n   142→    locality = first(locality),\n   143→    mean_a = mean(n_assemblages),\n   144→    sd_a = sd(n_assemblages),\n   145→    pct_coexist = mean(n_assemblages >= 2),\n   146→    .groups = \"drop\"\n   147→  )\n   148→\n   149→p1 <- loc_final |>\n   150→  ggplot(aes(locality, mean_a)) +"}]},"uuid":"d815b4e9-97ce-44ee-a84c-2c851c84a805","timestamp":"2026-03-24T03:07:32.289Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"e186687a-d3e9-4509-93d7-4ab84d73da48","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/michael/research/dark-forest-metaplastic","sessionId":"0b0542dd-4368-4365-bedd-e8ea67549597","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"bright-snacking-tide"}

{"parentUuid":"c368514b-e429-4210-8c35-2e85a3c55111","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"132c9ed5-fdb5-4736-b7bf-e4dd29d08457","agentId":"a2bb51445be360701","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01VXJfEvAct4y52bKBbWMQ6N","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→title: \"Coexistence Without Differentiation: The Self-Sealing Dynamics of Hebbian Individuation\"\n     3→author:\n     4→  - name: \"Michael Bean\"\n     5→format:\n     6→  html:\n     7→    toc: true\n     8→    code-fold: true\n     9→    fig-width: 7\n    10→    fig-height: 5\n    11→bibliography: references.bib\n    12→---\n    13→\n    14→```{r setup, include=FALSE}\n    15→source(\"_setup.R\")\n    16→```\n    17→\n    18→## Abstract\n    19→\n    20→Papers 1 and 2 established that optimization-free Hebbian dynamics produce spatial individuation and coexistence through encounter locality, but assemblages remain qualitative clones — individuation without differenciation. We investigate whether temporal environmental variation, anti-Hebbian lateral inhibition, or artificially maintained cross-assemblage connectivity can produce functional differentiation. Cross-assemblage edges vanish within 15 sessions (median) across 840 simulations spanning 7 localities and 6 anti-Hebbian strengths (up to $10\\times$ the Hebbian rate). When cross-assemblage edges are artificially maintained through continuous injection, two outcomes obtain: edges initialised at moderate-to-high weights are Hebbian-reinforced and absorbed into assemblages, producing monopoly; edges at near-threshold weights persist as cross-assemblage connections but produce no differentiation — anti-Hebbian decorrelation at these maintained connections *reduces* rather than increases assemblage divergence. Decay rate sensitivity analysis confirms that the coexistence regime occupies a narrow band ($\\lambda = 0.002$) between network death and monopoly. Across 1,400 simulations and 196,000 observations, no parameter combination produces differentiation. We identify this as a *self-sealing* property of Hebbian individuation operating through two distinct mechanisms: topological isolation (cross-assemblage edges decay) and functional absorption (maintained cross-assemblage edges are co-opted into assemblage structure). This constitutes an empirical decomposition of Deleuze's distinction between individuation and differenciation: the Hebbian substrate achieves the former and is structurally incapable of the latter — not because assemblages cannot interact, but because interaction produces merger rather than difference.\n    21→\n    22→## Introduction\n    23→\n    24→Deleuze [-@deleuze1994] distinguished *individuation* — the emergence of discrete entities from a pre-individual field — from *differenciation* — the production of qualitative difference between those entities. Papers 1 and 2 in this series demonstrated that optimization-free Hebbian substrates achieve individuation readily: spatial encounter locality produces stable, modular assemblages around energy hotspots. But these assemblages are spatial clones, not qualitatively different entities. They occupy different regions of the grid but develop identical internal structure — what we will call *crystalline individuation*, following Simondon [-@simondon1958], who used crystallisation as the paradigm of physical individuation where the same mechanism resolves identically at every nucleation site. We invoke the crystal not as a model of the individuation *process* — our assemblages nucleate independently rather than propagating from a seed — but as a characterisation of the *result*: identical structure everywhere, with no residual metastability for further individuation.\n    25→\n    26→This matters for artificial life and the philosophy of emergent agency. If the substrate can only produce copies — individuation without differenciation — then it cannot generate the heterogeneous ecology that characterises biological systems. The question is whether supplementary mechanisms can break the symmetry that produces cloning, or whether the Hebbian substrate is structurally incapable of differenciation.\n    27→\n    28→We test three interventions, escalating in strength:\n    29→\n    30→1. **Temporal environmental variation** — hotspot configurations alternate on a fixed period, inspired by Kashtan and Alon's [-@kashtan2005] modularity-under-variation prediction.\n    31→\n    32→2. **Anti-Hebbian lateral inhibition** — cross-assemblage connections are weakened when endpoints co-activate [@foldiak1990], at strengths up to $10\\times$ the Hebbian learning rate.\n    33→\n    34→3. **Artificially maintained cross-assemblage edges** — testing whether the obstacle is topological (edges don't exist) or functional (edges exist but don't produce differentiation).\n    35→\n    36→All three fail, but for different reasons. The substrate is *self-sealing* through two mechanisms: topological isolation (cross-assemblage edges decay to zero) and functional absorption (when edges are maintained, they are co-opted into assemblage structure, producing merger rather than differentiation). The finding is not merely that differentiation does not occur, but that the conditions required for it are structurally incompatible with Hebbian dynamics.\n    37→\n    38→## Background: Hebbian Learning and the PCA Fixed Point\n    39→\n    40→Hebbian learning strengthens connections between co-active nodes: $\\Delta w_{ij} = \\eta \\cdot a_i \\cdot a_j$. In the continuous case, this drives the weight vector toward the principal eigenvector of the input correlation matrix [@oja1982]. When multiple assemblages receive qualitatively similar input — energy from hotspots, modulated by Gaussian noise — they converge to the same eigenvector. This is why assemblages are clones: the learning rule is symmetric with respect to assemblage identity.\n    41→\n    42→Anti-Hebbian learning [@foldiak1990] weakens connections between co-active nodes in different populations: $\\Delta w_{ij} = -\\alpha \\cdot a_i \\cdot a_j$ for cross-population edges. In biological neural circuits, this produces decorrelation and functional specialisation. But it requires persistent connections between populations to operate on — and, as we will show, it requires those connections to carry a particular kind of signal.\n    43→\n    44→The critical question is whether cross-assemblage connections can persist in a Hebbian substrate with weight decay ($\\lambda$ per step), and if so, whether they can carry a decorrelation signal rather than being absorbed into the correlation structure of adjacent assemblages.\n    45→\n    46→In Deleuze's [-@deleuze1994] terms, the question is whether the substrate supports two kinds of repetition. *Bare repetition* reproduces instances of an identical type — each assemblage is another token of the same structure. *Complex repetition* produces novelty through the internal difference of the repeating process itself. Our substrate, as we will show, is trapped in bare repetition: every assemblage converges to the same attractor, and every attempt to introduce difference is either ignored (topological isolation) or absorbed into sameness (functional absorption).\n    47→\n    48→## Methods\n    49→\n    50→### Temporal Field Substrate\n    51→\n    52→We extend the MultiField substrate from Papers 1--2 with three mechanisms:\n    53→\n    54→1. **Config switching**: Two hotspot configurations alternate every $T = 50$ steps. Configuration A: $(0.2, 0.3)$, $(0.8, 0.3)$, $(0.5, 0.8)$; Configuration B: $(0.2, 0.3)$, $(0.3, 0.7)$, $(0.7, 0.7)$. One position is shared, two differ.\n    55→\n    56→2. **Anti-Hebbian decorrelation**: Every 50 steps, assemblages are re-detected via connected components in the strong-edge subgraph. For cross-assemblage edges: $\\Delta w_{ij} = -\\alpha \\cdot a_i \\cdot a_j$.\n    57→\n    58→3. **Edge injection with controlled initialisation**: At each step, up to $k$ new edges are created between randomly selected nodes in different assemblages, initialised at weight $w_0 \\in \\{10^{-4}, 0.1, 1.0\\}$. This tests whether the obstacle to differentiation is the absence of cross-assemblage edges or their inability to carry a differentiation signal.\n    59→\n    60→All other dynamics are unchanged from Paper 2. Grid: $20 \\times 20$ (400 nodes). Encounter locality $\\sigma = 0.10$. Weight decay $\\lambda = 0.002$/step. Pruning threshold $10^{-4}$.\n    61→\n    62→### Metrics\n    63→\n    64→**Cross-assemblage edge count**: Edges connecting nodes in different assemblages. The primary diagnostic.\n    65→\n    66→**Weight modularity** ($M$): Within-assemblage weight mass divided by total weight mass.\n    67→\n    68→**Centroid cosine distance**: Mean pairwise cosine distance between assemblage centroid weight vectors. 0 = clones, 1 = orthogonal. Replaces the classifier-based metric from preliminary analysis, which was ill-posed at the observed assemblage sizes (3--11 nodes in 400-dimensional weight space).\n    69→\n    70→Assemblage detection uses connected components in the strong-edge subgraph (edges above the 75th percentile of absolute weight). A sensitivity analysis across 50th, 75th, and 90th percentile thresholds (210 runs) produces identical assemblage counts ($\\pm 0.1$), confirming that the bimodal weight distribution (most edges near 0 or $\\pm w_{\\max}$) makes detection robust to threshold choice.\n    71→\n    72→### Experimental Design\n    73→\n    74→**Experiment 1** (Locality $\\times$ Anti-Hebbian): 7 localities $\\in \\{0.08, \\ldots, 0.20\\}$ $\\times$ 6 anti-Hebbian strengths $\\in \\{0, \\ldots, 0.50\\}$ $\\times$ 20 seeds = 840 simulations $\\times$ 200 sessions. Maps the parameter space and establishes the self-sealing timeline.\n    75→\n    76→**Experiment 2** (Edge Injection): 3 initialisation weights $\\in \\{10^{-4}, 0.1, 1.0\\}$ $\\times$ 2 injection rates $\\in \\{0, 10\\}$/step $\\times$ 3 anti-Hebbian strengths $\\times$ 20 seeds = 360 simulations $\\times$ 50 sessions at $\\sigma = 0.10$. Tests whether maintained cross-assemblage connectivity enables differentiation.\n    77→\n    78→**Experiment 3** (Decay Sensitivity): 5 decay rates $\\in \\{0.0005, \\ldots, 0.01\\}$ $\\times$ 2 anti-Hebbian strengths $\\times$ 20 seeds = 200 simulations $\\times$ 50 sessions. Tests whether the self-sealing result is sensitive to the decay parameter.\n    79→\n    80→Total: 1,400 simulations producing 196,000 session-level observations, distributed across a 68-CPU Ray cluster.\n    81→\n    82→## Results\n    83→\n    84→### Cross-Assemblage Edges Vanish Within 15 Sessions\n    85→\n    86→```{r edge-trajectory, fig.cap=\"Cross-assemblage edges vanish within 15 sessions at σ=0.10. The median self-sealing completion session is 14 (range: 3–23).\"}\n    87→d1 <- read_experiment(\"r1_locality_alpha\")\n    88→\n    89→d1_traj <- d1 |>\n    90→  filter(locality == 0.10, anti_hebbian_strength == 0.0, session <= 30) |>\n    91→  group_by(session) |>\n    92→  summarise(\n    93→    mean_cross = mean(cross_assemblage_edges),\n    94→    se_cross = sd(cross_assemblage_edges) / sqrt(n()),\n    95→    .groups = \"drop\"\n    96→  )\n    97→\n    98→ggplot(d1_traj, aes(x = session)) +\n    99→  geom_ribbon(aes(ymin = mean_cross - se_cross, ymax = mean_cross + se_cross),\n   100→              fill = pal[2], alpha = 0.3) +\n   101→  geom_line(aes(y = mean_cross), color = pal[2], linewidth = 1) +\n   102→  geom_hline(yintercept = 0, linetype = \"dashed\", color = \"grey50\") +\n   103→  labs(x = \"Session\", y = \"Cross-assemblage edges\",\n   104→       title = \"Cross-assemblage connectivity collapses within 15 sessions\",\n   105→       subtitle = \"σ = 0.10, α = 0, 20 seeds. Mean ± SE. Median seal at session 14.\")\n   106→```\n   107→\n   108→At $\\sigma = 0.10$ (the coexistence regime from Paper 2), cross-assemblage edges decline from 196 at session 1 to 15.8 at session 10 to near-zero by session 15. The median self-sealing completion session across all 840 Experiment 1 simulations is 14 (range: 3--23). At steady state, 1.1% of observations show transient non-zero cross-assemblage edges (max = 16), reflecting rare stochastic fluctuations rather than sustained connectivity.\n   109→\n   110→```{r cross-heatmap, fig.cap=\"Mean cross-assemblage edges at steady state across locality × anti-Hebbian strength. Near-zero everywhere.\"}\n   111→d1_late <- d1 |>\n   112→  filter(session > 150) |>\n   113→  group_by(locality, anti_hebbian_strength) |>\n   114→  summarise(mean_cross = mean(cross_assemblage_edges), .groups = \"drop\")\n   115→\n   116→ggplot(d1_late, aes(x = factor(locality), y = factor(anti_hebbian_strength),\n   117→                    fill = mean_cross)) +\n   118→  geom_tile(color = \"white\", linewidth = 0.5) +\n   119→  geom_text(aes(label = sprintf(\"%.1f\", mean_cross)), size = 3) +\n   120→  scale_fill_gradient(low = \"white\", high = pal[2], name = \"Cross-asm\\nedges\",\n   121→                      limits = c(0, 2)) +\n   122→  labs(x = \"Encounter locality (σ)\", y = \"Anti-Hebbian strength (α)\",\n   123→       title = \"Near-zero cross-assemblage edges at all parameter combinations\",\n   124→       subtitle = \"Sessions 150–200, 20 seeds per cell\")\n   125→```\n   126→\n   127→This pattern is universal across the parameter space. Anti-Hebbian decorrelation at strengths up to $\\alpha = 0.50$ ($10\\times$ the Hebbian learning rate) has no effect because cross-assemblage edges have already vanished.\n   128→\n   129→The mechanism is analytically predictable. An edge between nodes in different assemblages at locality $\\sigma = 0.10$ receives expected Hebbian reinforcement $\\eta \\cdot E[a_i \\cdot a_j] \\approx 0$ (since activations are driven by uncorrelated local energy sources), while decay is deterministic at rate $\\lambda = 0.002$/step. The edge dies with probability approaching 1 within $\\sim$$\\ln(w_0 / 10^{-4}) / \\lambda \\cdot 300$ sessions.\n   130→\n   131→### The Coexistence-Monopoly Gradient\n   132→\n   133→```{r coexistence-gradient, fig.cap=\"Assemblage count and largest assemblage size across locality.\"}\n   134→d1_coex <- d1 |>\n   135→  filter(session > 150, anti_hebbian_strength == 0.0) |>\n   136→  group_by(locality) |>\n   137→  summarise(\n   138→    mean_n = mean(n_assemblages), se_n = sd(n_assemblages) / sqrt(n()),\n   139→    mean_larg = mean(largest_assemblage), se_larg = sd(largest_assemblage) / sqrt(n()),\n   140→    .groups = \"drop\")\n   141→\n   142→p1 <- ggplot(d1_coex, aes(x = locality, y = mean_n)) +\n   143→  geom_pointrange(aes(ymin = mean_n - se_n, ymax = mean_n + se_n), color = pal[3]) +\n   144→  geom_line(color = pal[3]) +\n   145→  labs(x = \"Locality (σ)\", y = \"Assemblage count\", title = \"Coexistence declines with locality\")\n   146→p2 <- ggplot(d1_coex, aes(x = locality, y = mean_larg)) +\n   147→  geom_pointrange(aes(ymin = mean_larg - se_larg, ymax = mean_larg + se_larg), color = pal[5]) +\n   148→  geom_line(color = pal[5]) +\n   149→  labs(x = \"Locality (σ)\", y = \"Largest assemblage\", title = \"Monopoly increases with locality\")\n   150→p1 + p2"}]},"uuid":"884e3f38-d7a2-4e58-9d09-ae659f7d45ca","timestamp":"2026-03-24T03:07:33.196Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"c368514b-e429-4210-8c35-2e85a3c55111","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/michael/research/dark-forest-metaplastic","sessionId":"0b0542dd-4368-4365-bedd-e8ea67549597","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"bright-snacking-tide"}

{"parentUuid":"f66a4261-7b4f-4499-ab47-0bf20f34c898","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"132c9ed5-fdb5-4736-b7bf-e4dd29d08457","agentId":"a2bb51445be360701","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_018W8jRCT8u5iJXKWt3L7JPF","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→title: \"Local Homeostasis Enables Differentiation in Hebbian Substrates\"\n     3→subtitle: \"Critical Periods, Attractor Resilience, and the Limits of Turing Morphogenesis\"\n     4→author:\n     5→  - name: Michael\n     6→format:\n     7→  html:\n     8→    toc: true\n     9→    code-fold: true\n    10→    fig-width: 7\n    11→    fig-height: 5\n    12→bibliography: references.bib\n    13→---\n    14→\n    15→```{r setup, include=FALSE}\n    16→source(\"_setup.R\")\n    17→```\n    18→\n    19→## Abstract\n    20→\n    21→Papers 1--3 of this programme demonstrated that pure Hebbian substrates\n    22→produce individuation---assemblages emerge spontaneously from noise---but are\n    23→structurally incapable of differenciation: self-sealing eliminates the\n    24→prerequisites for lateral inhibition and inter-unit communication. Here we\n    25→test the theoretically motivated hypothesis that a Turing morphogenesis analog\n    26→(per-node metaplastic learning rate + diffusing inhibitor field) can break this\n    27→barrier. Under hard $\\eta$ bounds, the Turing mechanism fails completely:\n    28→inhibitor coupling is purely destructive regardless of sign, strength, or\n    29→coupling topology. Under soft $\\eta$ bounds, coupling is partially rescued---exhibiting the\n    30→U-shaped dose-response predicted by Turing theory---but remains significantly\n    31→inferior to a simpler mechanism. Replacing the global homeostatic target with\n    32→a *local* target---each node regulates toward its spatial neighbors' mean\n    33→activity---transforms the system without requiring any inter-assemblage\n    34→communication. Local homeostatic metaplasticity produces stable,\n    35→perturbation-resilient differentiation among initially identical assemblages,\n    36→sustained over 1000 sessions with no decay. Crucially, this differentiation\n    37→is not merely geometric: assemblages develop measurably different functional\n    38→profiles (response diversity), satisfying DeLanda's criterion for\n    39→differentiation of capacities [@delanda2006new]. The system exhibits critical\n    40→period dynamics: inter-assemblage coupling introduced after differentiation\n    41→preserves diversity, while coupling from the start destroys it. We interpret\n    42→these findings through a triple philosophical framework: Simondon's\n    43→transduction explains the mechanism, Deleuze's ontology of problems explains\n    44→why differentiation occurs, and DeLanda's capacity criterion distinguishes\n    45→genuine functional differentiation from mere spatial separation. The work\n    46→identifies a productive fracture: the critical period introduces an\n    47→irreversible temporality that Simondon accommodates and Deleuze resists, while\n    48→the functional probe reveals that even successful differentiation remains\n    49→parametric---different values of the same capacities, not qualitatively novel\n    50→kinds.\n    51→\n    52→\n    53→## Introduction\n    54→\n    55→The question motivating this programme is deceptively simple: *what is the\n    56→minimal substrate that produces genuine functional differentiation?* Not mere\n    57→spatial separation, not clonal repetition, but the emergence of qualitatively\n    58→different kinds from initially identical components.\n    59→\n    60→Papers 1--3 established the baseline. A Hebbian substrate---nodes on a 2D\n    61→grid connected by sparse, activity-dependent weights updated by a standard\n    62→Hebbian rule---spontaneously produces *individuation*: coherent assemblages\n    63→emerge from noise, consolidate through self-reinforcing weight dynamics, and\n    64→persist as distinct entities [@watson2016evolutionary]. But every assemblage is\n    65→a structural clone of every other. They differ in spatial position but not in\n    66→internal organisation, connectivity profile, or functional capacity.\n    67→\n    68→The mechanism responsible is *self-sealing*. As assemblages consolidate, they\n    69→strengthen internal connections and prune external ones. The self-reinforcing\n    70→Hebbian dynamic creates an absorbing boundary: once sealed, no local\n    71→perturbation can reopen the assemblage to external influence. Paper 3 tested\n    72→every intervention available within the Hebbian framework---anti-Hebbian\n    73→learning, cross-assemblage edge injection, temporal variation of the energy\n    74→landscape---and all failed. Self-sealing eliminates the two prerequisites for\n    75→differenciation identified by the pattern formation literature: lateral\n    76→inhibition and inter-unit communication [@turing1952chemical;\n    77→@gierer1972theory].\n    78→\n    79→In the Deleuzian framework that structures this programme, self-sealing\n    80→corresponds to *bare repetition*: the same intensive process applied\n    81→identically at multiple locations produces identical copies. *Complex\n    82→repetition*---differenciation---requires that the process itself change,\n    83→producing genuinely novel structures rather than spatial duplicates\n    84→[@deleuze1994difference; @delanda2002intensive].\n    85→\n    86→The natural hypothesis, then, is a Turing morphogenesis analog. If Hebbian\n    87→reinforcement acts as a short-range activator and a diffusing inhibitor field\n    88→acts as the long-range inhibitor, Turing instability at the *metaplastic*\n    89→level---modifying the learning rules themselves rather than the weights\n    90→directly---might break the symmetry that self-sealing preserves.\n    91→\n    92→This paper tests that hypothesis and finds a more complex answer than\n    93→anticipated. Under hard $\\eta$ bounds, the Turing mechanism fails completely\n    94→for structural reasons consistent with the network pattern formation\n    95→literature [@wolfrum2012turing; @nakao2010turing; @krause2024turing]. Under\n    96→soft $\\eta$ bounds, coupling is partially rescued, confirming that the\n    97→initial failure was partly an implementation artifact (hard $\\eta$ clipping\n    98→violates the continuity of intensive quantities that the Deleuzian framework\n    99→assumes). But\n   100→even with soft bounds, coupling remains inferior to a simpler, more robust\n   101→mechanism: local homeostatic targets that produce stable differentiation\n   102→without any inter-assemblage communication. The critical result is that\n   103→communication becomes constructive only *after* differentiation has been\n   104→established, exhibiting critical period dynamics analogous to those in\n   105→cortical development [@bienenstock1982theory; @sweeney2015diffusive]. A\n   106→functional probe confirms that the resulting differentiation is not merely\n   107→geometric: assemblages develop distinct signal amplification profiles,\n   108→partially satisfying DeLanda's criterion for differentiation of capacities\n   109→[@delanda2006new].\n   110→\n   111→\n   112→## Methods\n   113→\n   114→### Substrate\n   115→\n   116→The MetaplasticField extends the MultiField substrate from Paper 2. Nodes are\n   117→arranged on a 2D grid (default 20 $\\times$ 20 = 400 nodes). Energy sources\n   118→(hotspots) drive spatially varying noise injection. Weights are sparse,\n   119→updated by the Hebbian rule, and pruned below a threshold. Activity-dependent\n   120→encounters create new connections biased toward spatial neighbours, governed\n   121→by a locality parameter.\n   122→\n   123→### Metaplastic learning rate\n   124→\n   125→Each node $i$ maintains its own learning rate $\\eta_i$, initialised\n   126→identically to the global $\\eta = 0.05$. The Hebbian update for edge\n   127→$(i, j)$ uses the average: $\\eta_{ij} = \\tfrac{1}{2}(\\eta_i + \\eta_j)$.\n   128→\n   129→A homeostatic adjustment modifies $\\eta_i$ each step:\n   130→\n   131→$$\\Delta\\eta_i = -\\alpha \\cdot (\\bar{a}_i - \\tau_i)$$\n   132→\n   133→where $\\alpha$ is the metaplastic strength, $\\bar{a}_i$ is the exponential\n   134→moving average of activity history (default rate $= 0.05$, i.e.\\ 95\\% old +\n   135→5\\% new, following the conventional value used in homeostatic plasticity\n   136→models [@sweeney2015diffusive]; Exp 18 confirms robustness across an order\n   137→of magnitude), and $\\tau_i$ is the homeostatic target.\n   138→\n   139→Two target regimes are compared:\n   140→\n   141→- **Global target** (original): $\\tau_i = 0.15$ for all nodes.\n   142→- **Local target** (corrective): $\\tau_i = \\text{mean}(\\bar{a}_j : j \\in\n   143→  \\mathcal{N}_r(i))$, where $\\mathcal{N}_r(i)$ is the set of grid neighbours\n   144→  within Manhattan radius $r$.\n   145→\n   146→Learning rates are bounded: $\\eta_i \\in [0.005, 0.20]$. Two bounding\n   147→regimes are compared: **hard clipping** ($\\eta_i$ set to the nearer bound\n   148→when exceeded) and **soft bounding** (tanh saturation that asymptotically\n   149→approaches but never reaches the bounds). Weights are always hard-clipped\n   150→at $w_\\text{max}$ regardless of $\\eta$-bounding regime. This distinction"}]},"uuid":"80cf8eae-fd97-41e4-9fc0-59133775b31c","timestamp":"2026-03-24T03:07:33.402Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"f66a4261-7b4f-4499-ab47-0bf20f34c898","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/michael/research/dark-forest-metaplastic","sessionId":"0b0542dd-4368-4365-bedd-e8ea67549597","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"bright-snacking-tide"}

{"parentUuid":"c0cf243b-26e5-4a4d-95fd-aca0dc46cd2e","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"132c9ed5-fdb5-4736-b7bf-e4dd29d08457","agentId":"a2bb51445be360701","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01DrMjQmVQ8VLTKBbZKfX7B9","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→\"\"\"Multi-Field Substrate — multiple energy sources in 2D space.\n     2→\n     3→Extended from dark-forest-silica to support four weight bounding strategies:\n     4→  - hard: np.clip (Papers 1-4 baseline)\n     5→  - tanh: smooth saturation\n     6→  - sigmoid: smooth saturation (sharper transition)\n     7→  - oja: self-normalising Oja rule (replaces Hebbian update)\n     8→\"\"\"\n     9→\n    10→import numpy as np\n    11→from collections import defaultdict\n    12→\n    13→BOUND_TYPES = (\"hard\", \"tanh\", \"sigmoid\", \"oja\")\n    14→\n    15→\n    16→def _bound_weight_scalar(w, w_max, bound_type):\n    17→    \"\"\"Apply weight bound to a single scalar value.\"\"\"\n    18→    if bound_type == \"hard\":\n    19→        return np.clip(w, -w_max, w_max)\n    20→    elif bound_type == \"tanh\":\n    21→        return w_max * np.tanh(w / w_max)\n    22→    elif bound_type == \"sigmoid\":\n    23→        return 2.0 * w_max * (1.0 / (1.0 + np.exp(-2.0 * w / w_max))) - w_max\n    24→    return w  # oja — no explicit bound\n    25→\n    26→\n    27→class MultiField:\n    28→    \"\"\"2D field of identical nodes with multiple energy hotspots.\"\"\"\n    29→\n    30→    def __init__(self, grid_size=20, n_hotspots=3, hotspot_radius=0.2,\n    31→                 hotspot_energy=0.3, base_noise=0.02, eta=0.05, lam=0.002,\n    32→                 w_max=1.0, encounter_rate=20, locality=0.15,\n    33→                 prune_threshold=1e-4, bound_type=\"hard\", seed=None):\n    34→\n    35→        if bound_type not in BOUND_TYPES:\n    36→            raise ValueError(f\"bound_type must be one of {BOUND_TYPES}, got {bound_type!r}\")\n    37→\n    38→        self.grid_size = grid_size\n    39→        self.n_nodes = grid_size * grid_size\n    40→        self.eta = eta\n    41→        self.lam = lam\n    42→        self.w_max = w_max\n    43→        self.base_noise = base_noise\n    44→        self.hotspot_energy = hotspot_energy\n    45→        self.hotspot_radius = hotspot_radius\n    46→        self.encounter_rate = encounter_rate\n    47→        self.locality = locality\n    48→        self.prune_threshold = prune_threshold\n    49→        self.bound_type = bound_type\n    50→        self.rng = np.random.default_rng(seed)\n    51→\n    52→        # 2D positions on [0,1] x [0,1]\n    53→        xs = np.linspace(0, 1, grid_size)\n    54→        ys = np.linspace(0, 1, grid_size)\n    55→        gx, gy = np.meshgrid(xs, ys)\n    56→        self.pos_x = gx.flatten()\n    57→        self.pos_y = gy.flatten()\n    58→\n    59→        # Place hotspots\n    60→        self.hotspots = self._place_hotspots(n_hotspots)\n    61→\n    62→        # Compute noise profile from hotspot distances\n    63→        self.noise_profile = self._compute_noise_profile()\n    64→\n    65→        # Activations\n    66→        self.activations = self.rng.uniform(-0.1, 0.1, self.n_nodes) + 0.1 * self.noise_profile\n    67→\n    68→        # Metrics\n    69→        self.step_count = 0\n    70→        self.edges_created = 0\n    71→        self.edges_pruned = 0\n    72→\n    73→        # Sparse weights\n    74→        self.weights = {}\n    75→        self._init_local_connections()\n    76→\n    77→        # Activity history\n    78→        self._activity_history = np.abs(self.activations.copy())\n    79→\n    80→    def _place_hotspots(self, n):\n    81→        \"\"\"Place hotspots spread across the field.\"\"\"\n    82→        if n == 1:\n    83→            return [(0.5, 0.5)]\n    84→        elif n == 2:\n    85→            return [(0.25, 0.5), (0.75, 0.5)]\n    86→        elif n == 3:\n    87→            return [(0.2, 0.3), (0.8, 0.3), (0.5, 0.8)]\n    88→        elif n == 4:\n    89→            return [(0.25, 0.25), (0.75, 0.25), (0.25, 0.75), (0.75, 0.75)]\n    90→        else:\n    91→            return [(self.rng.uniform(0.1, 0.9), self.rng.uniform(0.1, 0.9))\n    92→                    for _ in range(n)]\n    93→\n    94→    def _compute_noise_profile(self):\n    95→        \"\"\"Compute per-node noise level based on distance to nearest hotspot.\"\"\"\n    96→        profile = np.full(self.n_nodes, self.base_noise)\n    97→        for hx, hy in self.hotspots:\n    98→            dist = np.sqrt((self.pos_x - hx)**2 + (self.pos_y - hy)**2)\n    99→            contribution = self.hotspot_energy * np.exp(-dist**2 / (2 * self.hotspot_radius**2))\n   100→            profile += contribution"}]},"uuid":"2f313450-9e0d-4aa0-b15f-ffe5c69d0bf8","timestamp":"2026-03-24T03:07:59.493Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"c0cf243b-26e5-4a4d-95fd-aca0dc46cd2e","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/michael/research/dark-forest-metaplastic","sessionId":"0b0542dd-4368-4365-bedd-e8ea67549597","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"bright-snacking-tide"}

seed,\n    88→            \"session\": session,\n    89→            \"total_steps\": session * params[\"n_steps\"],\n    90→            \"bound_type\": params[\"bound_type\"],\n    91→ \"weight_max\": float(np.max(np.abs(w_flat))),\n    95→            \"saturation\": float(np.mean(np.abs(w_flat) > 0.99 * params[\"w_max\"])),\n    96→            \"mean_activation\": float(np.mean(np.abs(net.activations))),\n    97→            \"eta\": params[\"eta\"],\n    98→            \"lam\": params[\"lam\"],\n    99→        }\n   100→\n   101→        if prev_weights is not None:\n   102→            row[\"drift\"] = float(np.linalg.norm(w - prev_weights, \"fro\"))\n   103→        else:\n   104→            row[\"drift\"] = None\n   105→\n   106→        rows.append(row)\n   107→        prev_weights = w.copy()\n   108→\n   109→    os.makedirs(job_dir, exist_ok=True)\n   110→    pq.write_table(pa.Table.from_pylist(rows), job_file)\n   111→    return {\"condition\": condition, \"seed\": seed, \"n_rows\": len(rows)}\n   112→\n   113→\n   114→@ray.remote\n   115→def run_multifield_job(experiment_name, condition, seed, params, output_dir):\n   116→    \"\"\"Run one src.metrics.centroid_distance import centroid_cosine_distance\n   120→    import pyarrow as pa\n   121→    import pyarrow.parquet as pq\n   122→\n   123→    job_dir = os.path.join(output_dir, eta=params[\"eta\"],\n   135→        lam=params[\"lam\"],\n   136→        w_max=params[\"w_max\"],\n   137→        encounter_rate=params[\"encounter_rate\"],\n   138→        locality=params[\"locality\"],\n   139→        prune_threshold=params.get(\"prune_threshold\", 1e-4),\n   140→        bound_type=params[\"bound_type\"],\n   141→        seed=seed,\n   142→    )\n   143→\n   144→    rows = []\n   145→    save_sessions = params.get(\"save_weight_sessions\", [])\n   146→    weight_snapshot_rows = []\n   147→\n   148→    for session in range(1, params[\"n_sessions\"] + 1):\n   149→        for _ in range(params[\"n_steps\"]):\n   150→            mf.step()\n   151→\n   152→        asm = mf.find_assemblages()\n   153→        c = mf.census()\n   154→\n   155→        row = {\n   156→            \"experiment\": experiment_name,\n   157→            \"condition\": condition,\n   158→            \"seed\": seed,\n   159→            \"session\": \"mean_weight\": c[\"mean_weight\"],\n   164→            \"max_weight\": c[\"max_weight\"],\n   165→            \"mean_energy\": c[\"mean_energy\"],\n   166→            \"n_assemblages\": len(asm),\n   167→            \"largest_assemblage\": c[\"assemblage_sizes\"][0] if c[\"assemblage_sizes\"] else 0,\n   168→            \"modularity\": weight_modularity(mf.weights, asm),\n   169→            \"centroid_cosine_distance\": centroid_cosine_distance(mf.weights, asm, mf.n_nodes),\n   170→            \"locality\": float(params[\"locality\"]),\n   171→        }\n   172→\n   173→        # Exp 3 injection tracking\n   174→        if \"inject_session\" in params and session == params[\"inject_session\"]:\n   175→            if len(asm) >= 2:\n   176→                nodes_a = sorted(asm[0])\n   177→                nodes_b = sorted(asm[1])\n   178→                for _ in range(params.get(\"n_inject\", 10)):\n   179→                    ni = nodes_a[mf.rng.integers(0, len(nodes_a))]\n   180→                    nj = nodes_b[mf.rng.integers(0, len(nodes_b))]\n   181→                    if (ni, nj) not in mf.weights:\n   182→                        mf.weights[(ni, nj)] = 0.3\n   183→                        mf.edges_created += 1\n   184→            row[\"injection_event\"] = True\n   185→        else:\n   186→            row[\"injection_event\"] = False\n   187→\n   188→        # Cross-assemblage edge count\n   189→        if len(asm) >= 2:\n   190→            node_to_asm = {}\n   191→            for ai, nodes in enumerate(asm):\n   192→                for n in nodes:\n   193→                    node_to_asm[n] = ai\n   194→            cross_edges = sum(1 for (i, j) in mf.weights\n   195→                              if node_to_asm.get(i, -1) != node_to_asm.get(j, -1)\n   196→                              and node_to_asm.get(i, -1) >= 0\n   197→                              and node_to_asm.get(j, -1) >= 0)\n   198→            row[\"cross_assemblage_edges\"] = cross_edges\n   199→        else:\n   200→            row[\"cross_assemblage_edges\"] = 0\n   201→\n   202→        rows.append(row)\n   203→\n   204→        # Save weight snapshots for Exp 5\n   205→        if session in save_sessions:\n   206→            w_arr = np.array(list(mf.weights.values()))\n   207→            for wi, wv in enumerate(w_arr):\n   208→                weight_snapshot_rows.append({\n   209→                    \"experiment\": experiment_name,\n   210→                    \"condition\": condition,\n   211→                    \"seed\": seed,\n   212→                    \"session\": session,\n   213→                    \"bound_type\": params[\"bound_type\"],\n   214→                    \"weight_idx\": wi,\n   215→                    \"weight\": weight_snapshot_rows:\n   222→        snap_file = os.path.join(job_dir, f\"{condition}_seed{seed:04d}_weights.parquet\")\n   223→        pq.write_table(pa.Table.from_pylist(weight_snapshot_rows), snap_file)\n   224→\n   225→    return {\"condition\": condition, \"seed\": seed, \"n_rows\": len(rows)}\n   226→\n   227→\n   228→@ray.remote\n   229→def run_metaplastic_job(experiment_name, inhibitor_coupling=params[\"inhibitor_coupling\"],\n   263→        inhibitor_emission_rate=params.get(\"inhibitor_emission_rate\", 0.01),\n   264→        use_soft_bounds=params[\"use_soft_eta_bounds\"],\n   265→        weight_bound_type=params[\"weight_bound_type\"],\n   266→    )\n   267→\n   268→    rows = []\n   269→    for session in range(1, 275→        sizes = sorted([len(a) for a in asm], reverse=True)\n   276→\n   277→        pct_eta_at_min = float(np.mean(mf.node_eta <= mf.eta_min + 1e-6))\n   278→        pct_eta_at_max =       \"seed\": seed,\n   284→            \"session\": session,\n   285→            \"total_steps\": mf.step_count,\n   286→            \"weight_bound_type\": params[\"weight_bound_type\"],\n   287→            \"eta_bound_type\": \"soft\" if params[\"use_soft_eta_bounds\"] else \"hard\",\n   288→            \"n_edges\": len(mf.weights),\n   289→            \"modularity\": len(rows)}\n   312→\n   313→\n   314→# ============================================================\n   315→# Experiment builders\n   316→# ============================================================\n   317→\n   318→def build_exp1_regime(n_seeds=20):\n   319→    \"\"\"Exp 1: Three-regime structure. 4 bounds x 8 eta/lam x 20 seeds = 640.\"\"\"\n   320→    eta_lam_combos = [\n   321→        (0.005, 0.002), (0.01, 0.002), (0.02, 0.002), (0.05, 0.002),\n   322→        (0.02, 0.0005), (0.02, 0.001), (0.02, 0.005), (0.02, 0.01),\n   323→    ]\n   324→    jobs = []\n   325→    for bt in BOUND_TYPES:\n   326→        for eta, lam in eta_lam_combos:\n   327→            for seed in range(n_seeds):\n   328→                condition = f\"{bt}_eta{eta:.3f}_lam{lam:.4f}\"\n   329→                jobs.append((\"exp1_regime\", condition, seed, {\n   330→                    \"n_nodes\": 64, \"eta\": eta, \"lam\": lam, \"w_max\": 1.0,\n   331→                    \"bound_type\": bt, \"n_sessions\": 20, \"n_steps\": 1000,\n   332→                    \"noise_scale\": 5.0,\n   333→                }))\n   334→    return \"exp1_regime\", jobs, \"network\"\n   335→\n   336→\n   337→def build_exp2_coexistence(n_seeds=20):\n   338→    \"\"\"Exp 2: Coexistence/monopoly. 4 bounds x 7 localities x 20 seeds = 560.\"\"\"\n   339→    localities = [0.05, 0.08, 0.10, 0.15, 0.20, 0.30, 0.50]\n   340→    jobs = []\n   341→    for bt in BOUND_TYPES:\n   342→        for loc in localities:\n   343→            for seed in range(n_seeds):\n   344→                condition = f\"{bt}_loc{loc:.2f}\"\n   345→                params = dict(BASE_PARAMS)\n   346→                params[\"bound_type\"] = bt\n   347→                params[\"locality\"] = loc\n   348→                params[\"n_sessions\"] = 200\n   349→                params[\"n_steps\"] = 300\n   350→                jobs.append((\"exp2_coexistence\", condition, seed, params))\n   351→    return \"exp2_coexistence\", jobs, \"multifield\"\n   352→\n   353→\n   354→def build_exp3_self_sealing(n_seeds=20):\n   355→    \"\"\"Exp 3: Self-sealing. 4 bounds x 2 conditions x 20 seeds = 160.\"\"\"\n   356→    jobs = []\n   357→    for bt in BOUND_TYPES:\n   358→        for inject in [False, True]:\n   359→            for seed in range(n_seeds):\n   360→                tag = \"inject\" if inject else \"control\"\n   361→                condition = f\"{bt}_{tag}\"\n   362→                params = dict(BASE_PARAMS)\n   363→                params[\"bound_type\"] = bt\n   364→                params[\"locality\"] = 0.10\n   365→                params[\"n_sessions\"] = 200\n   366→                params[\"n_steps\"] = 300\n   367→                if inject:\n   368→                    params[\"inject_session\"] = 100\n   369→                    params[\"n_inject\"] = 10\n   370→                jobs.append((\"exp3_self_sealing\", condition, seed, params))\n   371→    return \"exp3_self_sealing\", jobs, \"multifield\"\n   372→\n   373→\n   374→def build_exp4_continuous(n_seeds=20):\n   375→    \"\"\"Exp 4: Fully continuous. 4 weight bounds x 2 eta bounds x 20 seeds = 160.\"\"\"\n   376→    jobs = []\n   377→    for wbt in BOUND_TYPES:\n   378→        for soft_eta in [False, True]:\n   379→            for seed in
