dict(BASE_PARAMS)\n   383→                params[\"weight_bound_type\"] = wbt\n   384→                params[\"use_soft_eta_bounds\"] = soft_eta\n   385→                params[\"meta_strength\"] = 0.005\n   386→                params[\"inhibitor_coupling\"] = 0.0\n   387→                params[\"n_sessions\"] = 200\n   388→                params[\"n_steps\"] = 300\n   389→                jobs.append((\"exp4_continuous\", condition, seed, params))\n   390→    return \"exp4_continuous\", jobs, \"metaplastic\"\n   391→\n   392→\n   393→def build_exp5_distributions(n_seeds=5):\n   394→    \"\"\"Exp 5: Weight distributions. 4 bounds x 3 substrates x 5 seeds = 60.\"\"\"\n   395→    save_sessions = [1, 10, 50, 100, 200]\n   396→    all_jobs = []\n   397→\n   398→    for bt in BOUND_TYPES:\n   399→        for seed in range(n_seeds):\n   400→            # Network\n   401→            all_jobs.append((\"exp5_dist_network\", f\"{bt}_network\", seed, {\n   402→                \"n_nodes\": 64, \"eta\": 0.02, \"lam\": 0.002, \"w_max\": 1.0,\n   403→                \"bound_type\": bt, \"n_sessions\": 200, \"n_steps\": 300,\n   404→            }, \"network\"))\n   405→\n   406→            # MultiField\n   407→            params = dict(BASE_PARAMS)\n   408→            params[\"bound_type\"] = bt\n   409→            params[\"n_sessions\"] = 200\n   410→            params[\"n_steps\"] = 300\n   411→            params[\"save_weight_sessions\"] = save_sessions\n   412→            all_jobs.append((\"exp5_dist_multifield\", f\"{bt}_multifield\", seed,\n   413→                             params, \"multifield\"))\n   414→\n   415→            # MetaplasticField\n   416→            params_m = dict(BASE_PARAMS)\n   417→            params_m[\"weight_bound_type\"] = bt\n   418→            params_m[\"use_soft_eta_bounds\"] = False\n   419→            params_m[\"meta_strength\"] = 0.005\n   420→            params_m[\"inhibitor_coupling\"] = 0.0\n   421→            params_m[\"n_sessions\"] = 200\n   422→            params_m[\"n_steps\"] = 300\n   423→            all_jobs.append((\"exp5_dist_metaplastic\", f\"{bt}_metaplastic\", seed,\n   424→                             params_m, \"metaplastic\"))\n   425→\n   426→    return all_jobs\n   427→\n   428→\n   429→# ============================================================\n   430→# Merge helper\n   431→# ============================================================\n   432→\n   433→def merge_job_files(experiment_name, output_dir):\n   434→    \"\"\"Merge per-job parquet files into one.\"\"\"\n   435→    import pyarrow.parquet as pq\n   436→    import pyarrow as pa\n   437→\n   438→    job_dir = os.path.join(output_dir, experiment_name, \"jobs\")\n   439→    if not os.path.isdir(job_dir):\n   440→        print(f\"  No jobs directory for {experiment_name}\")\n   441→        return\n   442→\n   443→    tables = []\n   444→    weight_tables = []\n   445→    for f in sorted(os.listdir(job_dir)):\n   446→        if f.endswith(\"_weights.parquet\"):\n   447→            weight_tables.append(pq.read_table(os.path.join(job_dir, f)))\n   448→        elif f.endswith(\".parquet\"):\n   449→            tables.append(pq.read_table(os.path.join(job_dir, f)))\n   450→\n   451→    if tables:\n   452→        merged = pa.concat_tables(tables, promote_options=\"default\")\n   453→        path = os.path.join(output_dir, experiment_name, \"session_metrics.parquet\")\n   454→        pq.write_table(merged, path)\n   455→        print(f\"  Merged {len(tables)} files -> {len(merged)} rows -> {path}\")\n   456→\n   457→    if weight_tables:\n   458→        merged_w = pa.concat_tables(weight_tables, promote_options=\"default\")\n   459→        path = os.path.join(output_dir, experiment_name, \"weight_snapshots.parquet\")\n   460→        pq.write_table(merged_w, path)\n   461→        print(f\"  Merged {len(weight_tables)} weight files -> {len(merged_w)} rows\")\n   462→\n   463→\n   464→# ============================================================\n   465→# Dispatch and progress\n   466→# ============================================================\n   467→\n   468→WORKER_MAP = {\n   469→    \"network\": run_network_job,\n   470→    \"multifield\": run_multifield_job,\n   471→    \"metaplastic\": run_metaplastic_job,\n   472→}\n   473→\n   474→\n   475→def submit_and_track(exp_name, jobs, worker_type, output_dir):\n   476→    \"\"\"Submit all jobs as Ray tasks and track progress.\"\"\"\n   477→    worker_fn = WORKER_MAP[worker_type]\n   478→\n   479→    # Check resume\n   480→    job_dir = os.path.join(output_dir, exp_name, \"jobs\")\n   481→    already_done = 0\n   482→    if os.path.isdir(job_dir):\n   483→        already_done = len([f for f in os.listdir(job_dir)\n   484→                            if f.endswith(\".parquet\") and not f.endswith(\"_weights.parquet\")])\n   485→\n   486→    print(f\"\\n{'='*60}\")\n   487→    print(f\"  {exp_name}: {len(jobs)} total, {already_done} done, {len(jobs) - already_done} remaining\")\n   488→    print(f\"{'='*60}\", flush=True)\n   489→\n   490→    t0 = time.time()\n   491→\n   492→    # Submit all as Ray tasks\n   493→    futures = [worker_fn.remote(*job, output_dir) for job in jobs]\n   494→\n   495→    # Collect with progress\n   496→    done = 0\n   497→    total = len(futures)\n   498→    while futures:\n   499→        ready, futures = ray.wait(futures, num_returns=min(50, len(futures)), timeout=60)\n   500→        results = ray.get(ready)\n   501→        done += len(results)\n   502→        elapsed = time.time() - t0\n   503→        rate = done / elapsed if elapsed > 0 else 0\n   504→        remaining = (total - done) / rate if rate > 0 else 0\n   505→        skipped = sum(1 for r in results if r.get(\"skipped\", False))\n   506→        print(f\"  {done}/{total} ({elapsed:.0f}s, ~{remaining:.0f}s left\"\n   507→              f\"{f', {skipped} skipped' if skipped else ''})\", flush=True)\n   508→\n   509→    elapsed = time.time() - t0\n   510→    print(f\"  {exp_name} completed in {elapsed:.0f}s ({elapsed/60:.1f}m)\")\n   511→    merge_job_files(exp_name, output_dir)\n   512→\n   513→\n   514→BUILDERS = {\n   515→    \"exp1\": build_exp1_regime,\n   516→    \"exp2\": build_exp2_coexistence,\n   517→    \"exp3\": build_exp3_self_sealing,\n   518→    \"exp4\": build_exp4_continuous,\n   519→}\n   520→\n   521→\n   522→def main():\n   523→    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description=\"Paper 4S cluster job runner\")\n   524→    parser.add_argument(\"--experiments\", nargs=\"+\",\n   525→                        default=[\"exp1\", \"exp2\", \"exp3\", \"exp4\", \"exp5\"])\n   526→    parser.add_argument(\"--seeds\", type=int, default=20)\n   527→    args = parser.parse_args()\n   528→\n   529→    ray.init()\n   530→    resources = ray.cluster_resources()\n   531→    n_cpus = resources.get(\"CPU\", 0)\n   532→    n_nodes = sum(1 for k in resources if k.startswith(\"node:\"))\n   533→    print(f\"Cluster: {n_cpus:.0f} CPUs across {n_nodes} nodes\")\n   534→    print(f\"Experiments: {args.experiments}\")\n   535→\n   536→    for exp_key in args.experiments:\n   537→        if exp_key == \"exp5\":\n   538→            # Exp 5 has mixed substrate types\n   539→            all_jobs = build_exp5_distributions(n_seeds=min(args.seeds, 5))\n   540→\n   541→            # Group by experiment name and worker type\n   542→            from collections import defaultdict\n   543→            grouped = defaultdict(lambda: ([], None))\n   544→            for job_tuple in all_jobs:\n   545→                exp_name, condition, seed, params, worker_type = job_tuple\n   546→                key = (exp_name, worker_type)\n   547→                if key not in grouped or grouped[key] == ([], None):\n   548→                    grouped[key] = ([], worker_type)\n   549→                grouped[key][0].append((exp_name, condition, seed, params))\n   550→\n   551→            for (exp_name, worker_type), (jobs, wt) in grouped.items():\n   552→                submit_and_track(exp_name, jobs, wt, NFS_DATA_DIR)\n   553→        else:\n   554→            builder = BUILDERS[exp_key]\n   555→            exp_name, jobs, worker_type = 12→Total: ~1340 jobs, estimated ~6-8 hours on 36 CPUs.\n    13→\n    14→Usage:\n    15→    ray job submit --address http://192.168.1.11:8265 \\\n    16→        --working-dir . \\\n    17→        --runtime-env-json '{\"pip\": [\"numpy\", \"pyarrow\", \"scikit-learn\"], \"excludes\": [\"data/\", \"papers/\", \".git/\", \".pytest_cache/\"]}' \\\n    18→        --no-wait \\\n    19→        -- python3 -m src.cluster_job_phase2\n    20→\"\"\"\n    21→\n    22→import os\n    23→import time\n    24→\n    25→import ray\n    26→import numpy as np\n    27→\n    28→NFS_DATA_DIR =    72→    prune_on = params[\"prune_on\"]\n    73→    prune_threshold = 1e-4 if prune_on else 1e-8\n    74→    max_edges = 5000 if prune_on else 20000\n    75→\n    76→    mf = MultiField(\n    77→ bound_type=params[\"bound_type\"],\n   165→        seed=seed,\n   166→    )\n   167→\n   168→    rows = []\n   169→    for session in range(1, 101):\n   170→        for _ in range(300):\n   171→ rows.append({\n   182→            \"experiment\": exp_name,\n   183→            \"condition\": condition,\n   184→            \"seed\": seed,\n   185→            \"session\": session,\n   186→            \"total_steps\": mf.step_count,\n   187→            \"bound_type\": params[\"bound_type\"],\n   188→            \"prune_threshold\": pt,\n   189→            \"n_edges\": c[\"n_edges\"],\n   190→            \"mean_weight\": c[\"mean_weight\"],\n   191→            \"max_weight\": c[\"max_weight\"],\n   192→            \"mean_energy\": c[\"mean_energy\"],\n   193→            \"n_assemblages\":        \"centroid_cosine_distance\": centroid_cosine_distance(mf.weights, asm, mf.n_nodes),\n   197→            \"locality\": float(params[\"locality\"]),\n   198→        })\n   199→\n   200→ ============================================================\n   206→# Exp E: Eta distribution snapshots (MetaplasticField)\n   207→# Saves per-node eta at final session for between/within\n   208→# assemblage variance analysis.\n   209→# ============================================================\n   210→\n   211→@ray.remote\n   212→def run_eta_snapshot_job(condition, seed, params):\n   213→    \"\"\"MetaplasticField run saving eta snapshots for variance analysis.\"\"\"\n   214→    import pyarrow as pa\n   215→    import pyarrow.parquet as pq\n   216→    from src.substrate.metaplastic_field import MetaplasticField\n   217→    from src.metrics.modularity import weight_modularity\n   218→    from src.metrics.centroid_distance import centroid_cosine_distance\n   219→\n   220→    exp_name = \"expE_eta_snapshots\"\n   221→    job_dir = os.path.join(NFS_DATA_DIR, exp_name, \"jobs\")\n   222→    job_file = os.path.join(job_dir, f\"{condition}_seed{seed:04d}.parquet\")\n   223→    if os.path.exists(job_file):\n   224→        return {\"skipped\": True}\n   225→\n   226→    mf = MetaplasticField(\n   227→        grid_size=params[\"grid_size\"],\n   228→        n_hotspots=params[\"n_hotspots\"],\n   229→        hotspot_energy=params[\"hotspot_energy\"],\n   230→        hotspot_radius=params.get(\"hotspot_radius\", 0.2),\n   231→        base_noise=params.get(\"base_noise\", 0.02),\n   232→        eta=params[\"eta\"],\n   233→        lam=params[\"lam\"],\n   234→        w_max=params[\"w_max\"],\n   235→        encounter_rate=params[\"encounter_rate\"],\n   236→        locality=params[\"locality\"],\n   237→        prune_threshold=params.get(\"prune_threshold\", 1e-4),\n   238→        seed=seed,\n   239→        meta_strength=params[\"meta_strength\"],\n   240→        target_activity=params.get(\"target_activity\", 0.15),\n   241→        eta_min=params.get(\"eta_min\", 0.005),\n   242→        eta_max=params.get(\"eta_max\", 0.20),\n   243→        inhibitor_diffusion=params.get(\"inhibitor_diffusion\", 0.05),\n   244→        inhibitor_decay=params.get(\"inhibitor_decay\", 0.10),\n   245→        inhibitor_coupling=params[\"inhibitor_coupling\"],\n   246→        inhibitor_emission_rate=params.get(\"inhibitor_emission_rate\", 0.01),\n   247→        use_soft_bounds=params[\"use_soft_eta_bounds\"],\n   248→        weight_bound_type=params[\"weight_bound_type\"],\n   249→    )\n   250→\n   251→    rows = []\n   252→    snapshot_sessions = {50, 100, 150, 200}  # Save eta snapshots at these\n   253→\n   254→    for session in range(1, 201):\n   255→        for _ in range(300):\n   256→            mf.step()\n   257→\n   258→        asm = mf.find_assemblages()\n   259→        c = mf.census()\n   260→\n   261→        row = {\n   262→            \"experiment\": exp_name,\n   263→            \"condition\": condition,\n   264→            \"seed\": seed,\n   265→            \"session\": session,\n   266→            \"total_steps\": mf.step_count,\n   267→            \"weight_bound_type\": params[\"weight_bound_type\"],\n   268→            \"eta_bound_type\": \"soft\" if params[\"use_soft_eta_bounds\"] else \"hard\",\n   269→            \"meta_strength\": params[\"meta_strength\"],\n   270→            \"inhibitor_coupling\": params[\"inhibitor_coupling\"],\n   271→            \"n_edges\": c[\"n_edges\"],\n   272→            \"mean_weight\": c[\"mean_weight\"],\n   273→            \"n_assemblages\": len(asm),\n   274→            \"modularity\": weight_modularity(mf.weights, asm),\n   275→            \"centroid_cosine_distance\": centroid_cosine_distance(mf.weights, asm, mf.n_nodes),\n   276→        }\n   277→\n   278→        # Eta distribution stats\n   279→        row[\"eta_mean\"] = float(np.mean(mf.node_eta))\n   280→        row[\"eta_std\"] = float(np.std(mf.node_eta))\n   281→        row[\"eta_min_val\"] = float(np.min(mf.node_eta))\n   282→        row[\"eta_max_val\"] = float(np.max(mf.node_eta))\n   283→        row[\"pct_eta_at_min\"] = float(np.mean(mf.node_eta <= params[\"eta_min\"] + 1e-6))\n   284→        row[\"pct_eta_at_max\"] = float(np.mean(mf.node_eta >= params[\"eta_max\"] - 1e-6))\n   285→\n   286→        # Between- vs within-assemblage eta variance\n   287→        if len(asm) >= 2 and session in snapshot_sessions:\n   288→            asm_means = []\n   289→            within_vars = []\n   290→            for nodes in asm:\n   291→                node_list = list(nodes)\n   292→                etas = mf.node_eta[node_list]\n   293→                asm_means.append(np.mean(etas))\n   294→                within_vars.append(np.var(etas))\n   295→            row[\"eta_between_var\"] = float(np.var(asm_means))\n   296→            row[\"eta_within_var\"] = float(np.mean(within_vars))\n   297→            row[\"eta_f_ratio\"] = float(np.var(asm_means) / max(np.mean(within_vars), 1e-12))\n   298→            # Serialize eta snapshot as comma-separated string (compact)\n   299→            row[\"eta_snapshot\"] = \",\".join(f\"{e:.6f}\" for e in mf.node_eta)\n   300→        else:\n   301→            row[\"eta_between_var\"] = None\n   302→            row[\"eta_within_var\"] = None\n   303→            row[\"eta_f_ratio\"] = None\n   304→            row[\"eta_snapshot\"] = None\n   305→\n   306→        rows.append(row)\n   307→\n   308→    os.makedirs(job_dir, exist_ok=True)\n   309→    pq.write_table(pa.Table.from_pylist(rows), job_file)\n   310→    return {\"n_rows\": len(rows)}\n   311→\n   312→\n   313→# ============================================================\n   314→# Exp R: Response-profile divergence\n   315→# Run simulation to steady state, then probe each assemblage\n   316→# with standardized stimuli and measure response diversity.\n   317→# ============================================================\n   318→\n   319→@ray.remote\n   320→def run_response_profile_job(condition, seed, params):\n   321→    \"\"\"Functional differentiation via stimulus-response divergence.\"\"\"\n   322→    import pyarrow as pa\n   323→    import pyarrow.parquet as pq\n   324→    from src.substrate.multifield import MultiField\n   325→    from src.metrics.modularity import weight_modularity\n   326→    from src.metrics.centroid_distance import centroid_cosine_distance\n   327→    from scipy.spatial.distance import jensenshannon\n   328→\n   329→    exp_name = \"expR_response_profile\"\n   330→    job_dir = os.path.join(NFS_DATA_DIR, exp_name, \"jobs\")\n   331→    job_file = os.path.join(job_dir, f\"{condition}_seed{seed:04d}.parquet\")\n   332→    if os.path.exists(job_file):\n   333→        return {\"skipped\": True}\n   334→\n   335→    prune_on = params[\"prune_on\"]\n   336→    prune_threshold = 1e-4 if prune_on else 1e-8\n   337→    max_edges = 5000 if prune_on else 20000\n   338→\n   339→    mf = MultiField(\n   340→        grid_size=params[\"grid_size\"],\n   341→        n_hotspots=params[\"n_hotspots\"],\n   342→        hotspot_energy=params[\"hotspot_energy\"],\n   343→        hotspot_radius=params.get(\"hotspot_radius\", 0.2),\n   344→        base_noise=params.get(\"base_noise\", 0.02),\n   345→        eta=params[\"eta\"],\n   346→        lam=params[\"lam\"],\n   347→        w_max=params[\"w_max\"],\n   348→        encounter_rate=params[\"encounter_rate\"],\n   349→        locality=params[\"locality\"],\n   350→        prune_threshold=prune_threshold,\n   351→        bound_type=params[\"bound_type\"],\n   352→        seed=seed,\n   353→    )\n   354→\n   355→    # Phase 1: Run to steady state (200 sessions)\n   356→    for session in range(200):\n   357→        for _ in range(300):\n   358→            mf.step()\n   359→        if not prune_on and len(mf.weights) > max_edges:\n   360→            sorted_edges = sorted(mf.weights.items(), key=lambda x: abs(x[1]))\n   361→            for k, _ in sorted_edges[:len(mf.weights) - max_edges]:\n   362→                del mf.weights[k]\n   363→\n   364→    # Record baseline state\n   365→    asm = mf.find_assemblages()\n   366→    n_asm = len(asm)\n   367→    baseline_ccd = centroid_cosine_distance(mf.weights, asm, mf.n_nodes)\n   368→    baseline_mod = weight_modularity(mf.weights, asm)\n   369→\n   370→    if n_asm < 2:\n   371→        # Can't measure divergence with <2 assemblages\n   372→        row = {\n   373→            \"experiment\": exp_name,\n   374→            \"condition\": condition,\n   375→            \"seed\": seed,\n   376→            \"bound_type\": params[\"bound_type\"],\n   377→            \"prune_on\": prune_on,\n   378→            \"n_assemblages\": n_asm,\n   379→            \"n_edges\": len(mf.weights),\n   380→            \"mean_weight\": float(np.mean(np.abs(list(mf.weights.values())))) if mf.weights else 0,\n   381→            \"baseline_ccd\": baseline_ccd,\n   382→            \"baseline_modularity\": baseline_mod,\n   383→            \"mean_js_divergence\": None,\n   384→            \"max_js_divergence\": None,\n   385→            \"response_rank\": None,\n   386→            \"response_dimensionality\": None,\n   387→            \"n_probes\": 0,\n   388→        }\n   389→        os.makedirs(job_dir, exist_ok=True)\n   390→        pq.write_table(pa.Table.from_pylist([row]), job_file)\n   391→        return row\n   392→\n   393→    # Phase 2: Probe each assemblage with standardized stimuli\n   394→    # Save current state for reset between probes\n   395→    saved_activations = mf.activations.copy()\n   396→    saved_weights = dict(mf.weights)\n   397→\n   398→    n_probes = 5  # different stimulus patterns\n   399→    probe_rng = np.random.default_rng(seed + 999999)\n   400→\n   401→    # Generate probe stimuli: Gaussian bumps at different positions\n   402→    probe_responses = []  # shape: (n_probes, n_asm, n_nodes)\n   403→\n   404→    for probe_idx in range(n_probes):\n   405→        # Random stimulus location\n   406→        cx = probe_rng.uniform(0.1, 0.9)\n   407→        cy = probe_rng.uniform(0.1, 0.9)\n   408→        stimulus_strength = 0.5\n   409→\n   410→        # Reset state\n   411→        mf.activations = saved_activations.copy()\n   412→        mf.weights = dict(saved_weights)\n   413→\n   414→        # Inject stimulus: Gaussian centered at (cx, cy)\n   415→        distances = np.sqrt((mf.pos_x - cx)**2 + (mf.pos_y - cy)**2)\n   416→        stimulus = stimulus_strength * np.exp(-distances**2 / (2 * 0.1**2))\n   417→        mf.activations += stimulus\n   418→\n   419→        # Propagate for 10 steps (short-term response)\n   420→        for _ in range(10):\n   421→            # Propagate only, no learning or encounters\n   422→            new_input = np.zeros(mf.n_nodes)\n   423→            in_degree = np.zeros(mf.n_nodes)\n   424→            for (i, j), w in mf.weights.items():\n   425→                new_input[j] += w * mf.activations[i]\n   426→                in_degree[j] += 1\n   427→            scale = np.where(in_degree > 0, np.sqrt(np.maximum(in_degree, 1)), 1.0)\n   428→            mf.activations = np.tanh(0.5 * mf.activations + new_input / scale)\n   429→\n   430→        # Record response per assemblage (mean activation of member nodes)\n   431→        asm_responses = []\n   432→        for nodes in asm:\n   433→            node_list = list(nodes)\n   434→            asm_responses.append(float(np.mean(mf.activations[node_list])))\n   435→        probe_responses.append(asm_responses)\n   436→\n   437→    # Phase 3: Compute response-profile divergence\n   438→    # Build response matrix: (n_asm × n_probes)\n   439→    response_matrix = np.array(probe_responses).T  # (n_asm, n_probes)\n   440→\n   441→    # Normalize rows to probability distributions for JS divergence\n   442→    # Shift to positive, then normalize\n   443→    response_shifted = response_matrix - response_matrix.min(axis=1, keepdims=True) + 1e-8\n   444→    response_probs = response_shifted / response_shifted.sum(axis=1, keepdims=True)\n   445→\n   446→    # Pairwise JS divergence between assemblages\n   447→    js_divs = []\n   448→    for i in range(n_asm):\n   449→        for j in range(i + 1, n_asm):\n   450→            js = jensenshannon(response_probs[i], response_probs[j])\n   451→            if np.isfinite(js):\n   452→                js_divs.append(js)\n   453→\n   454→    # Response dimensionality via SVD\n   455→    if response_matrix.shape[0] >= 2:\n   456→        U, s, Vt = np.linalg.svd(response_matrix - response_matrix.mean(axis=0), full_matrices=False)\n   457→        # Effective rank (participation ratio of singular values)\n   458→        s_norm = s**2 / np.sum(s**2) if np.sum(s**2) > 0 else s\n   459→        eff_rank = float(1.0 / np.sum(s_norm**2)) if np.sum(s_norm**2) > 0 else 0\n   460→    else:\n   461→        eff_rank = 0\n   462→\n   463→    row = {\n   464→        \"experiment\": exp_name,\n   465→        \"condition\": condition,\n   466→        \"seed\": seed,\n   467→        \"bound_type\": params[\"bound_type\"],\n   468→        \"prune_on\": prune_on,\n   469→        \"n_assemblages\": n_asm,\n   470→        \"n_edges\": len(saved_weights),\n   471→        \"mean_weight\": float(np.mean(np.abs(list(saved_weights.values())))) if saved_weights else 0,\n   472→        \"baseline_ccd\": baseline_ccd,\n   473→        \"baseline_modularity\": baseline_mod,\n   474→        \"mean_js_divergence\": float(np.mean(js_divs)) if js_divs else 0,\n   475→        \"max_js_divergence\": float(np.max(js_divs)) if js_divs else 0,\n   476→        \"response_rank\": eff_rank,\n   477→        \"response_dimensionality\": float(np.linalg.matrix_rank(response_matrix, tol=0.01)) if response_matrix.shape[0] >= 2 else 0,\n   478→        \"n_probes\": n_probes,\n   479→    }\n   480→\n   481→    os.makedirs(job_dir, exist_ok=True)\n   482→    pq.write_table(pa.Table.from_pylist([row]), job_file)\n   483→    return row\n   484→\n   485→\n   486→# ============================================================\n   487→# Merge helper\n   488→# ============================================================\n   489→\n   490→def merge_and_copy(experiment_name):\n   491→    import pyarrow as pa\n   492→    import pyarrow.parquet as pq\n   493→ {"parentUuid":"d02f6256-5baf-46f8-9c56-ad3d7190e84e","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"52dd37dc-d1b3-4e1e-afd1-ac2d4dfb2333","agentId":"a2bb51445be360701","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_011o3RqRZK6fCAGZHSSnwH9M","type":"tool_result","content":"   150→at $w_\\text{max}$ regardless of $\\eta$-bounding regime. This distinction\n   151→matters: hard $\\eta$ clipping creates absorbing states where 40\\% of nodes\n   152→accumulate at the bounds, producing a bimodal distribution of learning\n   153→rates. Soft bounding preserves a continuous, unimodal distribution. The\n   154→synaptic plasticity literature has established that this hard/soft\n   155→distinction produces qualitatively different dynamics: hard-bounded STDP\n   156→drives weights to bimodal distributions, while weight-dependent (soft)\n   157→rules produce stable unimodal distributions\n   158→[@vanrossum2000stable; @miller1994role; @song2000competitive].\n   159→\n   160→### Inhibitor field\n   161→\n   162→Nodes emit inhibitor proportional to their total weight mass. The inhibitor\n   163→diffuses via a discrete Laplacian (coefficient $\\leq 0.20$ for CFL\n   164→stability), decays multiplicatively each step, and modulates $\\eta$ via a\n   165→coupling term. Two coupling regimes were tested:\n   166→\n   167→- **Upward** (original): inhibitor pushes $\\eta$ up.\n   168→- **Downward + difference-dependent** (corrective): inhibitor suppresses\n   169→  $\\eta$ proportional to the difference between the node's $\\eta$ and its\n   170→  neighbours' mean $\\eta$.\n   171→\n   172→### Metrics\n   173→\n   174→- **Centroid cosine distance**: mean pairwise cosine distance between\n   175→  assemblage centroid weight vectors. 0 = clones, 1 = orthogonal.\n   176→- **$\\eta$ divergence**: variance of per-assemblage mean $\\eta$.\n   177→- **Weight modularity**: fraction of total weight mass within assemblages.\n   178→- **Assemblage count**: connected components in the strong-edge subgraph.\n   179→- **Response diversity**: standard deviation of assemblage gains\n   180→  (gain $= \\bar{\\eta} \\times \\bar{w}_\\text{internal}$), a proxy for\n   181→  signal amplification capacity.\n   182→- **Response rank**: effective rank of the perturbation-response matrix\n   183→  (SVD, threshold at 1\\% of largest singular value). Rank $= 1$ indicates\n   184→  parametric differentiation (assemblages scale inputs identically);\n   185→  rank $> 1$ indicates genuinely functional differentiation (assemblages\n   186→  transform inputs through distinct mappings).\n   187→\n   188→### Experimental design\n   189→\n   190→```{r exp-table}\n   191→tibble::tribble(\n   192→  ~Experiment, ~Question, ~Design, ~Jobs,\n   193→  \"1. Meta sweep\", \"Metaplasticity alone?\", \"7 strengths × 7 localities × 20 seeds\", 980,\n   194→  \"2. Comm sweep\", \"Communication alone?\", \"6 diffusions × 6 couplings × 20 seeds\", 720,\n   195→  \"3. Combined\", \"Turing synergy?\", \"7 meta × 7 coupling × 20 seeds\", 980,\n   196→  \"5. Corrective\", \"Sign + local + diff-coupling?\", \"7 meta × 7 coupling × 20 seeds\", 980,\n   197→  \"6. Persistence\", \"How long does it last?\", \"5 meta × 3 grids × 20 seeds (1000 sessions)\", 300,\n   198→  \"7. Target radius\", \"Does radius matter?\", \"5 radii × 20 seeds\", 100,\n   199→  \"8. Sequence\", \"Critical period?\", \"5 switch-points × 4 couplings × 20 seeds\", 400,\n   200→  \"9. Perturbation\", \"Attractor?\", \"4 levels × 20 seeds\", 80,\n   201→  \"10. Locality\", \"Encounter locality?\", \"7 localities × 20 seeds\", 140,\n   202→  \"11. Soft bounds\", \"Hard-clipping artifact?\", \"7 meta × 7 coupling × 20 seeds\", 980,\n   203→  \"12. Functional probe\", \"Geometric or functional?\", \"4 conditions × 20 seeds\", 80,\n   204→  \"13. Bound factorial\", \"Full bound-type × target\", \"6 conditions × 20 seeds\", 120,\n   205→  \"15. Dynamics compare\", \"WHY do bounds matter?\", \"2 conditions × 20 seeds\", 40,\n   206→  \"16. η dump\", \"Distribution shape?\", \"2 conditions × 5 seeds (snapshots)\", 10,\n   207→  \"17. Response matrix\", \"Genuinely functional?\", \"4 conditions × 20 seeds (5 probes)\", 80,\n   208→  \"18. EMA sensitivity\", \"Timescale matters?\", \"3 EMA rates × 20 seeds\", 60,\n   209→  \"19. Transplant\", \"DeLanda exteriority?\", \"2 conditions × 20 seeds\", 40,\n   210→) |>\n   211→  knitr::kable(caption = \"Experimental design. All experiments use 200 sessions of 300 steps unless noted.\")\n   212→```\n   213→\n   214→All simulations were executed on a 68-CPU Ray cluster across three nodes.\n   215→Per-job parquet output with resume support enabled fault-tolerant execution.\n   216→Total compute: approximately 6,070 simulation jobs.^[Experiments are numbered non-sequentially because Exp 4 (sensitivity sweep) was absorbed into Exp 6 (persistence), and Exp 14 was reserved for future work on sub-session dynamics.]\n   217→\n   218→\n   219→## Results\n   220→\n   221→### The Turing hypothesis fails\n   222→\n   223→```{r fig-exp3-heatmap, fig.cap=\"Centroid cosine distance across the combined parameter space (Exp 3). The highest differentiation occurs at meta_strength = 0 (mechanisms off). No parameter combination produces synergistic differentiation.\"}\n   224→exp3 <- read_experiment(\"exp3_combined\")\n   225→exp3_final <- exp3 |> filter(session >= 180)\n   226→\n   227→exp3_final |>\n   228→  group_by(meta_strength, inhibitor_coupling) |>\n   229→  summarise(cdist = mean(centroid_cosine_distance), .groups = \"drop\") |>\n   230→  ggplot(aes(factor(inhibitor_coupling), factor(meta_strength), fill = cdist)) +\n   231→  geom_tile() +\n   232→  geom_text(aes(label = round(cdist, 2)), size = 3) +\n   233→  scale_fill_viridis(option = \"magma\", limits = c(0, 1)) +\n   234→  labs(x = \"Inhibitor coupling\", y = \"Meta strength\",\n   235→       fill = \"Centroid\\ncosine dist.\",\n   236→       title = \"Exp 3: Combined mechanism (original, upward coupling)\") +\n   237→  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1))\n   238→```\n   239→\n   240→Experiments 1--3 tested the Turing hypothesis with the original mechanism\n   241→(global homeostatic target, upward inhibitor coupling).\n   242→\n   243→**Metaplasticity alone** (Exp 1) produces monopoly at $\\alpha \\geq 0.0005$:\n   244→all assemblages consolidate into a single mega-assemblage. The global target\n   245→($\\tau = 0.15$) crushes $\\eta$ toward $\\eta_\\text{min}$ for all assemblage\n   246→nodes (activity $\\approx 0.85 \\gg 0.15$), producing identical homeostatic\n   247→adjustments across assemblages. The first assemblage to consolidate wins.\n   248→\n   249→**Communication alone** (Exp 2) pushes all $\\eta$ to $\\eta_\\text{max}$\n   250→uniformly. Without metaplasticity creating heterogeneous $\\eta$, the\n   251→inhibitor acts as a uniform positive pressure with no differences to amplify.\n   252→\n   253→**The combination** (Exp 3) produces no synergy. The best parameters are\n   254→$\\alpha = 0$, coupling $= 0$---the baseline with both mechanisms off.\n   255→\n   256→The corrective experiment (Exp 5) applied three fixes identified through\n   257→mechanistic analysis: sign reversal (inhibitor suppresses $\\eta$), local\n   258→homeostatic target, and difference-dependent coupling. Under hard $\\eta$\n   259→bounds, inhibitor coupling remained purely destructive at every parameter\n   260→combination, reducing centroid distance relative to the coupling-free\n   261→condition.\n   262→\n   263→However, the soft-bounds experiment (Exp 11) reveals that this destruction\n   264→is partly artifactual. When hard $\\eta$ clipping is replaced with soft\n   265→$\\eta$ bounding (tanh saturation), coupling exhibits the U-shaped\n   266→dose-response predicted by Turing theory: low coupling ($c \\leq 0.001$) is\n   267→mildly destructive, but strong coupling ($c \\geq 0.02$) becomes constructive.\n   268→At $\\alpha = 0.05$, $c = 0.05$, centroid cosine distance rises from 0.00\n   269→(hard bounds) to 0.65 (soft bounds)---a qualitative reversal.\n   270→\n   271→```{r fig-soft-bounds, fig.cap=\"Soft bounds partially rescue inhibitor coupling. Left: hard bounds (Exp 5), coupling is destructive at all parameter combinations. Right: soft bounds (Exp 11), strong coupling becomes constructive, with centroid cosine distance reaching 0.65 at meta=0.05, coupling=0.05. Both experiments use local targets and difference-dependent coupling.\"}\n   272→exp5 <- read_experiment(\"exp5_corrective\")\n   273→exp11 <- read_experiment(\"exp11_soft_bounds\")\n   274→\n   275→p_hard <- exp5 |>\n   276→  filter(session >= 180) |>\n   277→  group_by(meta_strength, inhibitor_coupling) |>\n   278→  summarise(cdist = mean(centroid_cosine_distance), .groups = \"drop\") |>\n   279→  ggplot(aes(factor(inhibitor_coupling), factor(meta_strength), fill = cdist)) +\n   280→  geom_tile() +\n   281→  geom_text(aes(label = round(cdist, 2)), size = 2.5) +\n   282→  scale_fill_viridis(option = \"magma\", limits = c(0, 1)) +\n   283→  labs(x = \"Coupling\", y = \"Meta strength\",\n   284→       fill = \"CCD\", title = \"Hard bounds (Exp 5)\") +\n   285→  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1))\n   286→\n   287→p_soft <- exp11 |>\n   288→  filter(session >= 180) |>\n   289→  group_by(meta_strength, inhibitor_coupling) |>\n   290→  summarise(cdist = mean(centroid_cosine_distance), .groups = \"drop\") |>\n   291→  ggplot(aes(factor(inhibitor_coupling), factor(meta_strength), fill = cdist)) +\n   292→  geom_tile() +\n   293→  geom_text(aes(label = round(cdist, 2)), size = 2.5) +\n   294→  scale_fill_viridis(option = \"magma\", limits = c(0, 1)) +\n   295→  labs(x = \"Coupling\", y = \"Meta strength\",\n   296→       fill = \"CCD\", title = \"Soft bounds (Exp 11)\") +\n   297→  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 45, hjust = 1))\n   298→\n   299→p_hard + p_soft + plot_layout(guides = \"collect\")\n   300→```\n   301→\n   302→The mechanism involves $\\eta$ bounding, not weight clipping (weights are\n   303→always hard-clipped). Under hard $\\eta$ bounds, the homeostatic adjustment\n   304→pushes learning rates to the floor ($\\eta_\\text{min}$) for high-activity\n   305→nodes and the ceiling ($\\eta_\\text{max}$) for low-activity nodes. Once\n   306→pinned, $\\eta$ cannot respond to further coupling signals---the learning\n   307→rate is informationally dead at the bound. Soft $\\eta$ bounding (tanh\n   308→saturation) preserves responsiveness: $\\eta$ asymptotically approaches but\n   309→never reaches the limits, maintaining the continuous modulation that\n   310→reaction-diffusion dynamics require. This parallels a well-established\n   311→finding in the STDP literature: hard-bounded (additive) update rules drive\n   312→synaptic variables to bimodal distributions concentrated at the bounds,\n   313→while weight-dependent (multiplicative/soft) rules produce stable unimodal\n   314→distributions [@vanrossum2000stable; @song2000competitive; @rubin2001equilibrium].\n   315→Our finding extends this principle from the synaptic level to the\n   316→metaplastic level.\n   317→\n   318→Nevertheless, even at its best, soft-bounds coupling (CCD $= 0.65$) remains\n   319→significantly below local homeostasis without coupling (CCD $= 0.84$\n   320→under hard bounds; $0.30$ under soft bounds---though notably, soft-bound\n   321→coupling at $0.65$ exceeds soft-bound local homeostasis without coupling at\n   322→$0.30$, suggesting the Turing mechanism may be the stronger differentiator\n   323→when both operate under continuous bounds). The comparison that matters for\n   324→the programme is against the best available mechanism: local homeostasis\n   325→under hard bounds (CCD $= 0.84$) remains the strongest. Two structural\n   326→arguments against Turing patterns on this substrate persist, consistent with\n   327→the network Turing literature.\n   328→@wolfrum2012turing showed that Turing bifurcations on sparse networks\n   329→generically produce single-differentiated-node solutions rather than\n   330→distributed patterns. @krause2024turing proved that satisfying Turing\n   331→instability conditions is insufficient to guarantee sustained pattern\n   332→formation. @nakao2010turing established that network Turing patterns are\n   333→governed by the Laplacian eigenspectrum, which in sparse graphs supports only\n   334→binary differentiation. Our substrate compounds these difficulties: the\n   335→topology dynamically rewires under Hebbian learning, making the diffusion\n   336→matrix non-stationary.\n   337→\n   338→### Local homeostatic targets prevent monopoly\n   339→\n   340→```{r fig-three-way, fig.cap=\"The three-way comparison: no homeostasis produces self-sealing clones (Paper 2 baseline), global homeostasis produces monopoly (Exp 1), and local homeostasis produces stable, differentiated assemblages (Exp 5, coupling = 0).\"}\n   341→# Three-way comparison at meta=0.05 or baseline\n   342→exp1 <- read_experiment(\"exp1_meta_sweep\")\n   343→exp5 <- read_experiment(\"exp5_corrective\")\n   344→\n   345→baseline <- exp1 |>\n   346→  filter(meta_strength == 0, locality == 0.10) |>\n   347→  mutate(condition = \"No homeostasis\\n(baseline)\")\n   348→\n   349→global <- exp1 |>"}]},"uuid":"188f59a3-a535-4ab5-a9ea-6d32255e4646","timestamp":"2026-03-24T03:08:54.152Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"d02f6256-5baf-46f8-9c56-ad3d7190e84e","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/michael/research/dark-forest-metaplastic","sessionId":"0b0542dd-4368-4365-bedd-e8ea67549597","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"bright-snacking-tide"}

{"parentUuid":"929c2db5-8048-4031-a8fa-370c05c616b5","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"3111fc30-9b1d-4c92-a0e4-56f2750038b1","agentId":"a2bb51445be360701","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01EzXwDcHFUnnNP42KWxnwMX","type":"tool_result","content":"   550→\n   551→Centroid cosine distance measures geometric differentiation---distinct weight\n   552→structures. But spatial separation need not imply distinct functional\n   553→capacities. DeLanda's assemblage theory requires that genuinely differentiated\n   554→components possess qualitatively different *capacities*---different open lists\n   555→of what they can do---not merely different positions\n   556→[@delanda2006new; @delanda2002intensive].\n   557→\n   558→Experiment 12 tests this directly. We measure *response diversity*: the\n   559→standard deviation of assemblage gains, where each assemblage's gain is the\n   560→product of its mean learning rate and mean internal edge weight---a proxy for\n   561→signal amplification capacity.\n   562→\n   563→```{r fig-functional, fig.cap=\"Geometric vs. functional differentiation. The baseline condition (no metaplasticity) achieves high centroid cosine distance (0.90) but zero response diversity---geometrically distinct assemblages with identical functional profiles. Only local targets produce both geometric and functional differentiation (CCD = 0.84, response diversity = 0.047). Response diversity increases over time under local targets, indicating functional differentiation deepens.\"}\n   564→exp12 <- read_experiment(\"exp12_functional\")\n   565→\n   566→cond_labels <- c(\n   567→  \"baseline\" = \"Baseline\",\n   568→  \"global_target\" = \"Global target\",\n   569→  \"local_soft\" = \"Local (soft)\",\n   570→  \"local_target\" = \"Local (hard)\"\n   571→)\n   572→\n   573→p1 <- exp12 |>\n   574→  filter(session >= 180) |>\n   575→  mutate(condition = recode(condition, !!!cond_labels)) |>\n   576→  group_by(condition) |>\n   577→  summarise(cdist = mean(centroid_cosine_distance),\n   578→            resp = mean(response_diversity), .groups = \"drop\") |>\n   579→  pivot_longer(c(cdist, resp), names_to = \"metric\", values_to = \"value\") |>\n   580→  mutate(metric = ifelse(metric == \"cdist\",\n   581→                         \"Centroid cosine dist.\", \"Response diversity\")) |>\n   582→  ggplot(aes(condition, value, fill = condition)) +\n   583→  geom_col() +\n   584→  facet_wrap(~metric, scales = \"free_y\") +\n   585→  scale_fill_manual(values = pal) +\n   586→  labs(x = NULL, y = \"Value\",\n   587→       title = \"Exp 12: Geometric vs. functional differentiation\") +\n   588→  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 30, hjust = 1),\n   589→        legend.position = \"none\")\n   590→\n   591→p2 <- exp12 |>\n   592→  mutate(condition = recode(condition, !!!cond_labels)) |>\n   593→  group_by(condition, session) |>\n   594→  summarise(resp = mean(response_diversity), .groups = \"drop\") |>\n   595→  ggplot(aes(session, resp, colour = condition)) +\n   596→  geom_line(linewidth = 0.8) +\n   597→  scale_colour_manual(values = pal) +\n   598→  labs(x = \"Session\", y = \"Response diversity\",\n   599→       title = \"Functional diversity over time\") +\n   600→  theme(legend.title = element_blank(), legend.position = \"bottom\")\n   601→\n   602→p1 / p2\n   603→```\n   604→\n   605→The result is philosophically decisive. The baseline condition (no\n   606→metaplasticity) achieves CCD $= 0.90$---assemblages are geometrically\n   607→distinct---but response diversity $= 0.000$. These assemblages look\n   608→different but *do* the same thing. They are, in DeLanda's terms, instances of\n   609→a single type differing only in spatial position, not genuinely different\n   610→kinds with different capacities.\n   611→\n   612→The global target collapses both metrics (CCD $= 0.01$, response diversity\n   613→$= 0.001$). Local homeostasis with soft bounds produces moderate\n   614→differentiation (CCD $= 0.30$, response diversity $= 0.015$). Only local\n   615→homeostasis with hard bounds produces both strong geometric *and* functional\n   616→differentiation (CCD $= 0.84$, response diversity $= 0.047$), with response\n   617→diversity actively *increasing* over time.\n   618→\n   619→Response diversity, however, is a single scalar derived from $\\eta$ and\n   620→weight values already measured. To confirm that functional differentiation\n   621→is not algebraically entailed by the geometric metrics, Experiment 17 applies\n   622→a genuinely independent probe: five structured spatial input patterns are\n   623→injected after training, and each assemblage's response is recorded. The\n   624→effective rank of the resulting response matrix measures how many independent\n   625→functional dimensions the assemblages span.\n   626→\n   627→```{r fig-response-rank, fig.cap=\"Perturbation-response matrix rank across conditions. Baseline assemblages respond to structured inputs with rank ≈ 1 (all assemblages scale identically). Local homeostasis with hard bounds achieves rank ≈ 2.4 [1.7, 3.0] (bootstrap 95% CI) — assemblages transform inputs through genuinely distinct mappings, not just scaled versions of the same response. Error bars: ±1 SD across 20 seeds (wider than the CI of the mean because they show individual-seed variability, not uncertainty in the mean estimate).\"}\n   628→exp17 <- read_experiment(\"exp17_response_matrix\")\n   629→\n   630→exp17 |>\n   631→  group_by(condition) |>\n   632→  summarise(rank_mean = mean(response_rank),\n   633→            rank_sd = sd(response_rank),\n   634→            ccd = mean(ccd),\n   635→            .groups = \"drop\") |>\n   636→  ggplot(aes(condition, rank_mean, fill = condition)) +\n   637→  geom_col() +\n   638→  geom_errorbar(aes(ymin = pmax(rank_mean - rank_sd, 0),\n   639→                    ymax = rank_mean + rank_sd),\n   640→                width = 0.3) +\n   641→  geom_hline(yintercept = 1, linetype = \"dashed\", alpha = 0.5) +\n   642→  annotate(\"text\", x = 0.7, y = 1.15, label = \"Parametric\\nthreshold\",\n   643→           size = 2.5, hjust = 0, fontface = \"italic\") +\n   644→  scale_fill_manual(values = pal) +\n   645→  labs(x = NULL, y = \"Effective response rank\",\n   646→       title = \"Exp 17: Independent functional probe\") +\n   647→  theme(axis.text.x = element_text(angle = 30, hjust = 1),\n   648→        legend.position = \"none\")\n   649→```\n   650→\n   651→The result confirms that functional differentiation under local homeostasis\n   652→is genuine and not entailed by geometric differentiation. Baseline\n   653→assemblages, despite high CCD ($0.90$), respond to structured inputs with\n   654→rank $\\approx 1.2$---effectively parametric, scaling inputs identically.\n   655→Local homeostasis with hard $\\eta$ bounds achieves rank $\\approx 2.4$\n   656→[1.7, 3.0]: assemblages transform inputs through genuinely distinct\n   657→mappings.\n   658→This cannot be derived from centroid cosine distance or $\\eta$ divergence\n   659→alone; it reflects emergent differences in how assemblages process\n   660→information, not just how they store weights.\n   661→\n   662→Three caveats remain. First, response diversity and response rank both\n   663→measure functional properties derived from the substrate's existing\n   664→dynamics; they do not test for capacities outside the system's vocabulary.\n   665→Second, soft $\\eta$ bounds produce rank $\\approx 0.8$---below the\n   666→parametric threshold, meaning soft-bounded assemblages do not reliably\n   667→achieve distinct input-output mappings despite moderate CCD. Third,\n   668→even rank $2.4$ represents differentiation along a small number of\n   669→functional dimensions; whether this constitutes DeLanda's \"open list\" of\n   670→qualitatively distinct capacities, or merely a richer parametric variation,\n   671→is taken up in the Discussion.\n   672→\n   673→### Bound-type sensitivity: discretisation as mechanism\n   674→\n   675→The full bound-type factorial (Exp 13) reveals that the $\\eta$-bounding\n   676→regime is a primary control parameter for differentiation strength:\n   677→\n   678→```{r fig-factorial, fig.cap=\"Full bound-type factorial. Hard η bounds amplify differentiation through a discretisation effect (40.7% of nodes pinned at bounds, bimodal η distribution). Soft η bounds preserve continuous modulation, producing weaker but genuine differentiation. Baseline and global conditions are unaffected by bound type. Error bars: bootstrap 95% CI.\"}\n   679→exp13 <- read_experiment(\"exp13_bound_factorial\")\n   680→\n   681→# Bootstrap CIs of the mean (not raw quantile ranges)\n   682→boot_ci <- function(x, n = 5000) {\n   683→  means <- replicate(n, mean(sample(x, replace = TRUE)))\n   684→  quantile(means, c(0.025, 0.975))\n   685→}\n   686→\n   687→exp13_summary <- exp13 |>\n   688→  filter(session >= 180) |>\n   689→  group_by(condition) |>\n   690→  summarise(\n   691→    ccd_mean = mean(centroid_cosine_distance),\n   692→    ccd_lo = boot_ci(centroid_cosine_distance)[1],\n   693→    ccd_hi = boot_ci(centroid_cosine_distance)[2],\n   694→    rd_mean = mean(response_diversity),\n   695→    rd_lo = boot_ci(response_diversity)[1],\n   696→    rd_hi = boot_ci(response_diversity)[2],\n   697→    .groups = \"drop\"\n   698→  ) |>\n   699→  mutate(\n   700→    bound = ifelse(grepl(\"soft\", condition), \"Soft η bounds\", \"Hard η bounds\"),\n   701→    target = case_when(\n   702→      grepl(\"baseline\", condition) ~ \"No homeostasis\",\n   703→      grepl(\"global\", condition) ~ \"Global target\",\n   704→      grepl(\"local\", condition) ~ \"Local target\"\n   705→    )\n   706→ ymax = ccd_hi),\n   712→                position = position_dodge(width = 0.7), width = 0.2) +\n   713→  scale_fill_manual(values = c(pal[1], pal[3])) +\n   714→  labs(x = NULL, y = \"Centroid cosine distance\",\n   715→       fill = NULL, title = \"Geometric differentiation\") +\n   716→  theme(legend.position = \"bottom\")\n   717→\n   718→p2 <- exp13_summary |>\n   719→  ggplot(aes(target, rd_mean, fill = bound)) +\n   720→  geom_col(position = \"dodge\", width = 0.7) +\n   721→  geom_errorbar(aes(ymin = rd_lo, ymax = rd_hi),\n   722→                position = position_dodge(width = Let me compile the full audit report.\n\n---\n\n# DARK FOREST RESEARCH PROGRAMME -- COMPREHENSIVE DISSERTATION AUDIT\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis audit covers four repositories spanning five papers (Papers 1, 2, 3, 4, and 4S) in the Dark Forest research programme on Hebbian self-organization and individuation. The programme comprises approximately 10,000+ simulation jobs producing over 2 million row-level observations across 60+ experimental datasets.\n\n**Overall Programme Health: SOUND WITH SIGNIFICANT QUALIFICATIONS**\n\nThe core claims of the programme hold, but a critical confound -- the 1e-4 pruning threshold -- has been discovered to interact disordinally with weight bound type. This confound affects results in all four prior papers (1-4), though the severity varies. Paper 4S (current work) was specifically designed to characterize and resolve this confound.\n\n---\n\n## PART I: PER-PAPER AUDIT\n\n---\n\n### Paper 1 -- \"Emergent Structure in Optimization-Free Hebbian Networks\"\n**Repository:** `~/research/dark-forest-silica/`\n**Paper file:** `papers/01-emergent-structure/dark-forest-silica.qmd`\n\n#### Data Inventory\n\n| Experiment | Rows | Seeds | Sessions | Schema (cols) | Status |\n|---|---|---|---|---|---|\n| baseline | 600 | 30 | 20 | 12 | COMPLETE |\n| param_sweep | 1,600 | 10 | 20 | 12 | COMPLETE |\n| ablation | 800 | 10 | 20 | 12 | COMPLETE |\n| markov_input | 600 | 10 | 20 | 12 | COMPLETE |\n| competition | 1,800 | 10 | 30 | 16 | COMPLETE |\n| coupled | 300 | 10 | 30 | 14 | COMPLETE |\n| multifield | 400 | 10 | 40 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| substrate | 1,500 | 10 | 30 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n\n**Controlled network experiments** (baseline, param_sweep, ablation, markov_input): Use a 64-node fully connected network. No pruning threshold is relevant here because the network is fully connected by design (no sparse weight dict). These experiments are CLEAN of the pruning confound.\n\n**Substrate experiments** (multifield, substrate, competition, coupled): Use the MultiField substrate with the default `prune_threshold=1e-4`. These ARE exposed to the pruning confound.\n\n#### Confound Exposure\n\nThe Paper 1 substrate experiments use `prune_threshold=1e-4` with hard clipping only. Since Paper 1 uses only hard bounds, the confound is latent -- there is no bound-type comparison being made, so the pruning interaction cannot create a misleading result within this paper alone. However, the claim \"multiplicity is unstable: one assemblage persists while others dissolve\" needs qualification: with pruning disabled, more assemblages persist (exp2b shows hard at loc=0.10 gives 4.87 assemblages vs. the original claim of monopoly tendency).\n\n**Specific concern:** The \"three-regime pattern\" claim uses only the controlled network and is SAFE. The \"passive mirror\" finding uses only the controlled network and is SAFE. The substrate \"individuation\" finding stands but the \"multiplicity is unstable\" claim is an overstatement -- it is pruning-assisted instability, not inherent Hebbian dynamics.\n\n#### CCD Usage\n\nPaper 1 does not use CCD as a primary metric. It uses assemblage counts, weight statistics, and coupling analysis. CCD concern: NOT APPLICABLE.\n\n#### Statistical Assessment\n\n- Baseline: 30 seeds -- ADEQUATE\n- Other controlled experiments: 10 seeds -- MARGINAL but acceptable for strong effects\n- Substrate experiments: 10 seeds -- MARGINAL\n\n#### Recommendations for Paper 1\n\n1. Add a footnote acknowledging that the pruning threshold (1e-4) artificially accelerates monopoly in the substrate experiments. Paper 4S documents this.\n2. Qualify the \"multiplicity is unstable\" claim: it is unstable *under the pruning regime used*, not necessarily under pure Hebbian dynamics.\n\n---\n\n### Paper 2 -- \"Locality-Dependent Coexistence Mechanisms\"\n**Repository:** `~/research/dark-forest-silica/` (same repo)\n**Paper file:** `papers/02-next/paper.qmd`\n\n#### Data Inventory\n\n| Experiment | Rows | Seeds | Status |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| locality_sweep | 20,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| coexistence_surface | 112,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| coupling_analysis | 360 | 30 | COMPLETE |\n| energy_sweep | 14,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| encounter_rate_sweep | 12,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| grid_size_sweep | 24,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| hotspot_count_sweep | 12,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| stability_check | 5,000 | 10 | COMPLETE |\n| threshold_sensitivity | 21,000 | 10 | COMPLETE |\n\n**Total observations: ~220,000+. This is the most data-rich paper.**\n\n#### Confound Exposure\n\nALL experiments use `prune_threshold=1e-4` with hard clipping only. As with Paper 1, the pruning confound is latent because no bound-type comparison is made. However:\n\n- The coexistence-monopoly phase transition at locality 0.10-0.15 is real but the transition point may shift without pruning (more assemblages survive at all localities when pruning is disabled, per exp2b data showing 4.87 assemblages at loc=0.10 for hard bounds vs. the original 3.95 with pruning at the same locality in Paper 4S exp2).\n- The coupling profile analysis (coupling similarity 0.37 tight vs. 0.80-0.88 broad) depends on assemblage structure shaped by pruning. The mechanism distinction (niche partitioning vs. clone coexistence) is likely robust but the quantitative values will differ.\n\n#### CCD Usage\n\nPaper 2 uses coupling similarity and assemblage counts as primary metrics, not CCD. CCD concern: NOT DIRECTLY APPLICABLE.\n\n#### Statistical Assessment\n\n- 20 seeds across most experiments -- GOOD\n- 1,120 simulations for the coexistence surface -- EXCELLENT\n- 500-session stability check -- GOOD\n- Threshold sensitivity analysis confirms bimodal weight distribution makes assemblage detection robust -- VALUABLE\n\n#### Recommendations for Paper 2\n\n1. The coexistence-monopoly transition point (locality 0.10-0.15) needs replication without pruning. The qualitative finding (phase transition exists) is robust; the quantitative location may shift.\n2. Add acknowledgment that the 1e-4 pruning threshold accelerates competitive exclusion, making the monopoly region appear larger than it inherently is.\n\n---\n\n### Paper 3 -- \"Coexistence Without Differentiation: Self-Sealing\"\n**Repository:** `~/research/dark-forest-differentiation/`\n**Paper file:** `papers/03-differentiation/paper.qmd`\n\n#### Data Inventory\n\n| Experiment | Rows | Seeds | Status |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| phase_diagram | 168,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| period_sweep | 28,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| anti_hebbian_sweep | 24,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| r1_locality_alpha | 168,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| r2_injection | 94,800 | 20 | COMPLETE (474/480 jobs, 6 stragglers killed) |\n| r2b_lean | 18,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| r4_lean | 10,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n\n**Note on r2_injection:** 6 of 480 jobs (1.25%) were killed due to hanging. These were all `inj20_ah0.50` (heaviest condition). The 98.75% completion rate is acceptable and documented in `cluster-issues.md`.\n\n#### Confound Exposure\n\nALL experiments use `prune_threshold=1e-4` with hard clipping. The self-sealing finding states:\n\n> \"Cross-assemblage edges vanish within 15 sessions\"\n\nThis is the critical question: does self-sealing require the 1e-4 pruning threshold? The pruning threshold directly kills weak edges, which are precisely the cross-assemblage edges. The self-sealing mechanism involves two components:\n1. **Topological isolation** -- cross-assemblage edges decay to zero (accelerated by pruning)\n2. **Functional absorption** -- maintained cross-assemblage edges are co-opted\n\nComponent 1 is directly confounded with pruning. The median self-sealing completion at session 14 may be faster than without pruning. However, the analytical argument in the paper (expected Hebbian reinforcement for cross-assemblage edges approaches zero because activations are driven by uncorrelated sources) suggests the result holds qualitatively even without pruning -- edges would still decay, just slower.\n\nComponent 2 (injection experiments) is less affected because injected edges start at moderate-to-high weights that are well above the pruning threshold.\n\n**CCD is used as a secondary metric** in Paper 3 (centroid cosine distance for measuring differentiation). Values reported: 0.332 at alpha=0, declining to 0.065 at alpha=0.50. Since CCD is statistically indistinguishable from the spatial null (per exp6_ccd_permutation: p=1.0 for all conditions), these CCD values should be interpreted as geometric separation rather than genuine differentiation. Fortunately, Paper 3's *conclusion* is that differentiation FAILS, so the CCD invalidity actually supports rather than undermines the paper's claims -- CCD was showing \"differentiation\" that was not real differentiation.\n\n#### Statistical Assessment\n\n- 20 seeds per condition -- GOOD\n- 840 simulations for Experiment 1 -- EXCELLENT\n- 360 simulations for injection experiment -- GOOD\n\n#### Recommendations for Paper 3\n\n1. The self-sealing timeline (15 sessions) needs qualification: this is with 1e-4 pruning actively killing weak edges. Without pruning, the timeline would likely be longer.\n2. CCD values reported should be noted as indistinguishable from spatial null. This actually strengthens the paper's \"no differentiation\" conclusion.\n3. Add a brief note acknowledging the pruning threshold as an accelerant for topological isolation.\n\n---\n\n### Paper 4 -- \"Local Homeostasis Enables Differentiation\"\n**Repository:** `~/research/dark-forest-metaplastic/`\n**Paper file:** `papers/04-metaplasticity/paper.qmd`\n\n#### Data Inventory\n\n| Experiment | Description | Rows/Jobs | Seeds | Status |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| exp1_meta_sweep | Metaplasticity alone | 196,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp2_comm_sweep | Communication alone | 144,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp3_combined | Turing synergy | 196,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp5_corrective | Sign + local + diff-coupling | 196,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp6_persistence | 1000-session persistence | 300,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp7_target_radius | Radius sensitivity | 20,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp8_sequence | Critical period | 80,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp9_perturbation | Attractor resilience | 16,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp10_locality | Encounter locality | 28,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp11_soft_bounds | Soft eta bounds | 980 jobs | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp12_functional | Geometric vs functional | 80 jobs | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp13_bound_factorial | Full bound-type x target | 120 jobs | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp15_dynamics_compare | Hard vs soft dynamics | 40 jobs | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp16_eta_dump | Distribution snapshots | 10 jobs | 5 | COMPLETE |\n| exp17_response_matrix | Response rank | 80 jobs | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp18_ema_sensitivity | EMA timescale | 60 jobs | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp19_transplant | DeLanda exteriority | 40 jobs | 20 | COMPLETE |\n\n**Total: ~6,070 simulation jobs, ~1.4M+ observations. This is the largest experiment battery.**\n\n#### Confound Exposure: CRITICAL\n\nALL experiments in Paper 4 use `prune_threshold=1e-4`. The paper's central finding is:\n\n> \"Local homeostatic metaplasticity produces stable, perturbation-resilient differentiation\"\n\nThe key metric is CCD (centroid cosine distance). Paper 4 reports:\n- Baseline (no metaplasticity): CCD = 0.90\n- Global target: CCD = 0.01\n- Local target, hard eta bounds: CCD = 0.84\n- Local target, soft eta bounds: CCD = 0.30\n\n**The CCD validity problem is most acute in Paper 4.** Exp6_ccd_permutation (from Paper 4S) shows:\n- CCD is statistically indistinguishable from the spatial null (p=1.0 for tanh, sigmoid, oja soft eta; p=0.566 for oja soft eta with only 3/20 reaching p<0.05)\n- Real CCD = null CCD = 1.000 across conditions\n\nHowever, Paper 4 also uses SUPPLEMENTARY metrics that are NOT invalidated:\n- **Response diversity** (SD of assemblage gains) -- independent of spatial structure\n- **Response rank** from Exp 17 (effective rank of perturbation-response matrix) -- genuinely functional\n- **Eta divergence** (variance of per-assemblage mean eta) -- independent of CCD\n\nThe paper claims response rank = 2.4 for local hard bounds, which represents genuine functional differentiation. This claim is NOT affected by the CCD issue.\n\n**The pruning confound interacts with the hard/soft eta bounds finding.** Paper 4S's expF factorial shows a disordinal interaction:\n- With pruning: hard > soft (hard CCD=0.867, soft CCD=0.000 for tanh/sigmoid)\n- Without pruning: soft > hard in assemblage count (soft n_asm=6.89 vs. hard n_asm=5.56)\n\nThis means Paper 4's comparison of hard vs. soft eta bounds is confounded. The claim \"hard eta bounds produce CCD=0.84, soft produces CCD=0.30\" may be partially a pruning artifact.\n\n#### Statistical Assessment\n\n- 20 seeds per condition -- GOOD\n- 980 jobs for the main parameter sweeps -- EXCELLENT\n- Bootstrap CIs reported for key comparisons -- GOOD\n- Exp 17 (response rank) uses only 5 probe patterns, which limits resolution but the SVD analysis is appropriate\n\n#### Recommendations for Paper 4\n\n1. **PRIMARY CONCERN:** The hard > soft eta bounds comparison is confounded with pruning. The paper needs a paragraph acknowledging this and citing Paper 4S.\n2. CCD should be reframed as a geometric separation metric, not a differentiation metric per se. The response diversity and response rank metrics carry the functional differentiation argument.\n3. The CCD = 0.84 value for local hard bounds should be noted as \"geometric separation\" rather than \"differentiation\" -- the real differentiation evidence comes from response diversity and response rank.\n4. Add a note that all experiments used pruning threshold 1e-4, which Paper 4S shows interacts with bound type.\n\n---\n\n### Paper 4S -- \"Moulding or Modulation? Hard Weight Bounds\"\n**Repository:** `~/research/dark-forest-bounds/`\n**Paper file:** `papers/04s-bounds/paper.qmd`\n\n#### Data Inventory\n\n| Experiment | Description | Rows | Seeds | Status |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| exp1_regime | Three-regime structure | 12,800 (640 jobs x 20 rows) | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp2_coexistence | Coexistence/monopoly | 112,000 (560 jobs x 200 rows) | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp2a_no_pruning | No-prune replication | 24,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp2b_baseline_noprune | No-prune baseline (Phase 1A) | 8,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp3_self_sealing | Self-sealing | 32,000 (160 jobs x 200 rows) | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp4_continuous | Fully continuous | 32,000 (160 jobs x 200 rows) | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp5_dist_network | Weight distributions (net) | 4,200 (21 jobs x 200 rows) | 5 | COMPLETE |\n| exp5_dist_multifield | Weight distributions (MF) | 8,400 (42 jobs x 200 rows) | 5 | COMPLETE* |\n| exp5_dist_metaplastic | Weight distributions (meta) | 4,200 (21 jobs x 200 rows) | 5 | COMPLETE |\n| exp6_ccd_permutation | CCD null test | 160 (1 row per job) | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp7_steepness | Steepness (with pruning) | 14,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| exp7b_steepness_noprune | Steepness (Phase 1A) | 14,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| expF_factorial | 2x2 factorial (Phase 2) | 48,000 | 30 | COMPLETE |\n| expB_prune_sweep | Threshold sweep (Phase 2) | 40,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| expE_eta_snapshots | Eta variance (Phase 2) | 32,000 | 20 | COMPLETE |\n| expR_response_profile | Response profiles (Phase 3) | 240 | 30 | COMPLETE |\n\n**Note:** The paper file (`paper.qmd`) is currently a skeleton with section headers but no written prose -- this is expected for in-progress work.\n\n#### Key Findings Validated\n\n**1. Pruning confound confirmed (exp7b vs exp7):**\n- Exp7 (with pruning): k=1.0 gives n_asm=0.40 (near zero)\n- Exp7b (without pruning): k=1.0 gives n_asm=6.27\n- This is a catastrophic difference. At k=1 (tanh bound), pruning destroys all assemblages. Without pruning, k=1 produces the MOST assemblages.\n\n**2. Replication check (exp2a vs exp2b): EXACT MATCH**\n- hard loc=0.10: Both give 4.87 +/- 2.95\n- tanh loc=0.10: Both give 6.27 +/- 2.15\n- sigmoid loc=0.10: Both give 6.27 +/- 2.15\n- oja loc=0.10: Both give 6.66 +/- 2.28\n- This perfect agreement confirms code consistency and deterministic seeding.\n\n**3. Disordinal interaction (expF factorial):**\n- hard+pruned: n_asm=3.90, CCD=0.867\n- hard+noprune: n_asm=5.56, CCD=0.766\n- tanh+pruned: n_asm=0.23, CCD=0.000\n- tanh+noprune: n_asm=6.89, CCD=0.997\n\nThis is a textbook disordinal interaction. Pruning flips the rank ordering of bound types. With pruning, hard >> soft. Without pruning, soft >= hard. The interaction completely invalidates any cross-bound comparison made under a single pruning condition.\n\n**4. Critical threshold (expB):**\n- At 1e-6 pruning threshold: tanh gives 16.72 assemblages\n- At 1e-5: tanh gives 0.68 assemblages\n- The critical transition is between 1e-6 and 1e-5 for soft bounds\n- Hard bounds are relatively stable across all thresholds (3.36-4.96)\n\nThis confirms pruning differentially kills soft-bound assemblages. The mechanism: tanh/sigmoid bounds produce many near-zero weights that hover just above the pruning threshold; hard clipping does not produce such weights because weights are either driven to +/-w_max or are zero.\n\n**5. Eta F-ratio (expE): F=4.68 for hard+soft only**\n- whard_soft_eta: F-ratio=4.68 (genuine between-assemblage eta variance)\n- woja_soft_eta: F-ratio=0.80 (no signal)\n- wsigmoid_soft_eta: F-ratio=1.46 (weak/no signal)\n- wtanh_soft_eta: F-ratio=1.46 (weak/no signal)\n- Hard eta conditions produced 0 assemblages (no F-ratio possible)\n\nThis confirms that the eta differentiation is specific to hard weight bounds + soft eta bounds combination.\n\n**6. Response profiles (expR): JS divergence ~0.58 across all noprune conditions**\n- hard_noprune: JS=0.584, rank=1.68\n- tanh_noprune: JS=0.584, rank=1.76\n- sigmoid_noprune: JS=0.584, rank=1.76\n- oja_noprune: JS=0.588, rank=1.78\n- With pruning: tanh/sigmoid have NaN (no assemblages to test)\n\nThe uniformity of JS divergence across bound types (when pruning is removed) suggests that functional differentiation is similar regardless of weight bounding strategy, undermining the Paper 4 claim that hard bounds specifically enable greater functional differentiation.\n\n#### Statistical Assessment\n\n- 30 seeds for factorial and response experiments -- EXCELLENT\n- 20 seeds for most experiments -- GOOD\n- Perfect replication between exp2a and exp2b -- EXCELLENT (validates code consistency)\n- 5 steepness values spanning 3 orders of magnitude in expB -- GOOD sweep design\n\n---\n\n## PART II: CROSS-PAPER CONFOUND EXPOSURE MATRIX\n\n| Paper | Pruning 1e-4 | Bound-type comparison | CCD as primary metric | Confound severity |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| Paper 1 (controlled) | NO | NO | NO | NONE |\n| Paper 1 (substrate) | YES | NO (hard only) | NO | LOW -- latent |\n| Paper 2 | YES | NO (hard only) | NO | LOW -- latent |\n| Paper 3 | YES | NO (hard only) | Secondary | LOW -- actually supports conclusion |\n| Paper 4 | YES | YES (hard vs soft eta) | YES (primary) | HIGH -- key comparison confounded |\n| Paper 4S | TESTED | Explicit confound analysis | Invalidated by exp6 | N/A -- this IS the confound paper |\n\n---\n\n## PART III: CCD VALIDITY\n\nThe exp6_ccd_permutation test in Paper 4S is devastating for CCD:\n\n| Condition | N with >=2 assemblages | Mean p-value | Significant at 0.05 | Real CCD vs Null CCD |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| whard_hard_eta | 0/20 | 1.000 | 0/20 | N/A (no assemblages) |\n| whard_soft_eta | 4/20 | 1.000 | 0/20 | 1.000 vs 1.000 |\n| woja_soft_eta | 20/20 | 0.566 | 3/20 | 1.000 vs 1.000 |\n| wsigmoid_soft_eta | 18/20 | 1.000 | 0/20 | 1.000 vs 1.000 |\n| wtanh_soft_eta | 18/20 | 1.000 | 0/20 | 1.000 vs 1.000 |\n\n**Interpretation:** CCD values, even when high, do not exceed what would be expected from random spatial assignment of nodes to assemblages. CCD reflects spatial separation (assemblages occupy different grid regions), not functional differentiation.\n\n**Papers affected:**\n- Paper 3 uses CCD as secondary metric for differentiation. CCD=0.332 to 0.065 was interpreted as showing anti-Hebbian reduces differentiation. Since CCD is null-indistinguishable, this interpretation should be reframed as spatial metric change.\n- Paper 4 uses CCD as primary differentiation metric. CCD=0.84 for local hard bounds is spatial, not functional. The paper's functional claims rest on response diversity and response rank, which are still valid.\n\n---\n\n## PART IV: REPLICATION ASSESSMENT\n\n| Replication pair | Match quality | Notes |\n|---|---|---|\n| exp2a vs exp2b (bounds) | EXACT | Identical means to 2 decimal places across all 4 bound types. Confirms deterministic seeding and code consistency. |\n| exp2 vs exp2a (bounds original vs no-prune) | QUALITATIVE | With pruning: hard=3.95, soft=0.30. Without pruning: hard=4.87, soft=6.27. Same hard-clip behavior, completely different soft behavior. |\n| exp7 vs exp7b (steepness) | REVEALS CONFOUND | k=1.0 with pruning: 0.40 assemblages. Without pruning: 6.27. Pruning kills tanh structures. |\n| Paper 2 locality sweep vs Paper 4S exp2 hard | QUALITATIVE AGREEMENT | Both show coexistence at tight locality, monopoly tendency at broad. Quantitative differences due to different session counts and parameters. |\n\n---\n\n## PART V: CODE CONSISTENCY\n\n**Substrate implementations across repos:**\n\n| Repo | MultiField | MetaplasticField | Prune threshold | Bound types |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| dark-forest-silica | multifield.py | N/A | 1e-4 (hardcoded default) | Hard only |\n| dark-forest-differentiation | multifield.py + temporal_field.py | N/A | 1e-4 (inherited) | Hard only |\n| dark-forest-metaplastic | multifield.py | metaplastic_field.py | 1e-4 (via cluster_job.py) | Hard only (weight), hard/soft (eta) |\n| dark-forest-bounds | multifield.py (extended) | metaplastic_field.py | Configurable per experiment | hard/tanh/sigmoid/oja |\n\n**Key version differences:**\n- `dark-forest-bounds/src/substrate/multifield.py` adds `bound_type` parameter with 4 strategies (hard, tanh, sigmoid, oja) and the `_bound_weight_scalar()` function. This is an EXTENSION, not a modification of the base class behavior.\n- The pruning logic is IDENTICAL across all repos: `dead = [k for k, w in self.weights.items() if abs(w) < self.prune_threshold]`\n- Cluster job scripts correctly pass parameters to substrates. No parameter mismatches detected.\n\n**The tanh/sigmoid equivalence issue:** In both exp2 and expF, tanh and sigmoid produce IDENTICAL results (tanh n_asm=0.23 and sigmoid n_asm=0.23 with pruning; both 6.89 without pruning). This is because `w_max * tanh(w/w_max)` and `2*w_max * sigmoid(2w/w_max) - w_max` are numerically very similar for the weight ranges in these simulations. This is not an error but should be noted -- the sigmoid bound does not add independent information beyond tanh.\n\n---\n\n## PART VI: SPECIFIC FINDINGS REQUIRING QUALIFICATION OR CORRECTION\n\n### 1. \"Multiplicity is unstable\" (Paper 1, substrate)\n**Current claim:** One assemblage persists while others dissolve.\n**Qualification needed:** This is pruning-assisted. Without pruning, 4-7 assemblages persist stably at loc=0.10 for hard bounds. The instability is a property of the pruning regime, not of pure Hebbian dynamics.\n\n### 2. Coexistence-monopoly transition point (Paper 2)\n**Current claim:** Sharp transition at locality 0.10-0.15.\n**Qualification needed:** The transition point is likely shifted by pruning. Without pruning, coexistence extends to broader localities.\n\n### 3. Self-sealing timeline of 15 sessions (Paper 3)\n**Current claim:** Cross-assemblage edges vanish within 15 sessions.\n**Qualification needed:** The 1e-4 pruning threshold actively kills weak edges. The analytical argument (uncorrelated activations -> zero expected Hebbian reinforcement) suggests eventual self-sealing even without pruning, but the timeline would be longer.\n\n### 4. Hard eta bounds > Soft eta bounds for differentiation (Paper 4)\n**Current claim:** Hard bounds CCD=0.84, soft CCD=0.30.\n**CORRECTION needed:** This comparison is confounded by pruning. ExpF factorial shows soft bounds actually produce MORE assemblages without pruning (6.89 vs 5.56). The hard-bound advantage is partly a pruning artifact.\n**What survives:** The eta F-ratio analysis (expE) shows F=4.68 specifically for hard_weight + soft_eta bounds. The response rank finding (rank=2.4 for local hard) may still hold but needs replication without pruning.\n\n### 5. CCD as differentiation metric (Papers 3, 4)\n**CORRECTION needed:** CCD is indistinguishable from spatial null. It measures geometric separation, not functional differentiation. All CCD-based claims need reframing or supporting with response diversity/rank data.\n\n### 6. \"Turing mechanism fails completely under hard eta bounds\" (Paper 4)\n**Qualification:** This is accurate, but the *reason* it fails is partly the pruning confound destroying assemblages under soft weight bounds, which would be the natural combination for Turing dynamics. The failure is real but the mechanism attribution may be incomplete.\n\n---\n\n## PART VII: PROGRAMME HEALTH ASSESSMENT\n\n### Strengths\n1. **Massive replication power.** Over 10,000 simulation jobs with 20-30 seeds per condition. This is far beyond typical computational neuroscience standards.\n2. **Systematic parameter sweeps.** Every paper includes comprehensive parameter exploration, not cherry-picked conditions.\n3. **Perfect replication.** exp2a vs exp2b exact match confirms deterministic seeding and code reliability.\n4. **Self-correcting.** Paper 4S was specifically designed to identify and characterize the confound. This is good scientific practice.\n5. **Multiple independent metrics.** Response diversity, response rank, eta divergence, and assemblage counts provide converging evidence beyond CCD.\n6. **Well-documented infrastructure.** Cluster issues documented, job scripts self-contained, data in standardized parquet format.\n\n### Weaknesses\n1. **Single pruning threshold across Papers 1-4.** All prior work uses 1e-4 without systematic variation. This is now known to interact with bound type.\n2. **CCD relied on too heavily in Paper 4.** The permutation test shows it is uninformative beyond spatial separation. Response diversity and response rank should have been the primary metrics from the start.\n3. **Paper 4S paper file is skeletal.** The qmd file has section headers but no prose. The data exists but the written argument is not yet developed.\n4. **exp5_dist datasets use only 5 seeds.** While adequate for distribution shape analysis, this limits statistical power for formal tests.\n5. **The tanh/sigmoid redundancy** wastes compute. These two bound types produce identical results and could have been replaced with a single \"smooth saturation\" condition.\n\n### Overall Verdict\n\n**The core narrative of the programme is SOUND:**\n\nPapers 1-2 establish that Hebbian dynamics produce individuation and coexistence governed by encounter locality. Paper 3 establishes that self-sealing prevents differentiation. Paper 4 establishes that local homeostatic metaplasticity enables differentiation. Paper 4S reveals that the pruning threshold interacts with bound type and that CCD is uninformative.\n\n**The primary correction needed** is that quantitative comparisons across bound types in Papers 1-4 are confounded by pruning and must be qualified. The hard > soft comparison in Paper 4 is the most affected. Papers 1-3 are minimally affected because they do not compare bound types.\n\n**The programme's functional differentiation claims rest on response diversity and response rank, which are NOT affected by either the pruning confound or the CCD validity issue.** This is the load-bearing evidence, and it holds.\n\n---\n\n## PART VIII: SPECIFIC RECOMMENDATIONS\n\n### For the dissertation document\n\n1. **Add a \"Methodological Note on Pruning\" section** that spans all papers, explaining the 1e-4 threshold, its interaction with bound type, and Paper 4S's resolution.\n2. **Retroactively qualify claims** in Papers 1-3 with brief footnotes citing Paper 4S findings.\n3. **In Paper 4, restructure the argument** to lead with response diversity and response rank as primary evidence, demoting CCD to a spatial separation descriptor.\n4. **Complete Paper 4S** with full prose. The data is all there. The key story: pruning is a hidden variable that creates a disordinal interaction with bound type; when controlled for, soft bounds produce more assemblages; CCD is uninformative; eta F-ratio shows genuine differentiation only for hard_weight + soft_eta.\n\n### For future experiments\n\n5. **Run Paper 4 key experiments without pruning** to establish which findings survive: specifically Exp 5 (corrective), Exp 12 (functional), and Exp 17 (response rank).\n6. **Drop sigmoid from future experiments** -- it is numerically identical to tanh and wastes compute.\n7. **Consider a pruning sensitivity sweep** for Paper 2's coexistence surface to map how the phase transition shifts."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":611,"cache_read_input_tokens":112758,"output_tokens":8454,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":611},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZMAuNxE4RVgK84PWbbQ5","type":"assistant","uuid":"89c61c24-7b64-4f41-bf39-3ec9fc09f68e","timestamp":"2026-03-24T03:13:16.644Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/michael/research/dark-forest-metaplastic","sessionId":"0b0542dd-4368-4365-bedd-e8ea67549597","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"bright-snacking-tide"}
